**Equivocal returns.** There are scattered appearances that function as ghost, vision, cosmic echo, or alternate-continuity counterpart — including Heralds of Galactus assemblages (the *Galactus the Devourer* / *Cosmic Powers* legacy material), the *Earth X* projection (where her counterpart appears in the Krigari/Herald registers in Ross/Krueger's mythological mode), and the *Marvel Zombies* / *Cancerverse* / *Ultimate* variants where Heralds are catalogued. None of these are her. They are uses of her iconography.

---

## 4.3 Present-Day Status

**Vital status:** deceased, primary 616 continuity, since 1992. No confirmed resurrection.

**Physical remains:** dispersed. Decapitation by cosmic-scale energy weapon at Power-Cosmic durability thresholds does not leave a corpse in the recoverable sense. There is no grave, no body, no shrine. This is consistent with — and perhaps the final expression of — the bodily dispossession theme that runs from Horton's lab forward: her body was never wholly hers, and at the end there is none of it left to be anyone's.

**Memorial status:** functionally none on Earth. Johnny Storm has had decades of subsequent romantic and team entanglements; she does not appear in his recurring grief register the way Alicia Masters or other long-term partners do. The Fantastic Four as an institution has not erected, named, or dedicated anything to her memory. This is itself diagnostic of her position in life: she was Johnny's girlfriend during a specific window, then she was Galactus's, and the Fantastic Four's institutional memory tracks her as a transitional figure rather than a member.

**Memorial status, cosmic:** somewhat greater. Among the Heralds and Herald-adjacent figures (Surfer foremost, Firelord in passing, Stardust ideologically) she is the recurring cautionary referent — *the one who embraced it*. Surfer in particular carries her as a moral counterweight in his internal monologues across multiple runs: she is what he would have become had he made different choices, and her existence proves the choice was real. In this sense she is not forgotten; she is *load-bearing*, posthumously, for someone else's character arc. A surveillance reader will note that even in death she is being curated by a more powerful figure — Surfer's narrative — exactly as she was curated by Horton, Johnny, and Galactus in life.

**Reputational status, in-universe:**
- **Among the Fantastic Four:** affectionate but distant memory; "Johnny's old girlfriend who became a Herald."
- **Among the Skrull Empire's survivors:** a war criminal of cosmic rank, named in their accounting of the Galactus depredations. If a Skrull intelligence service kept its own version of this file, her entry would be much shorter and much harsher.
- **Among the cosmic powers (Eternity, the Living Tribunal's order, the Watchers themselves):** a herald who served and was consumed by service. Standard pattern. Not exceptional in their register.
- **Among the surviving Heralds:** a sister, a warning, an embarrassment, or an ideal, depending on which one you ask. Stardust would have admired her. Firelord regards Herald-service ambivalently. Surfer, definitively, regards her as a failure of his — both his failure to dissuade her and his failure, earlier, to refuse the same path she chose.

**Reputational status, out-of-universe (editorial):** a closed canon. Writers approach her as a finished arc, which is exceptionally rare in superhero comics and which constitutes, in itself, a form of respect — the resistance to revive is the recognition that her story *cost* something to tell and would be cheapened by reversal.

---

## 4.4 How She Got Here: The Through-Line, Compressed

Tracing the surveillance file end-to-end produces a sequence of recategorizations of the same person by successively larger figures, each accepted by the subject as liberation:

1. **Child** → **experimental subject** (Horton, non-consensual, ~ages roughly 5–12 in the implied timeline).
2. **Experimental subject** → **amnesiac civilian with engineered phobia** (Horton's conditioning, ~age 12 onward).
3. **Civilian** → **girlfriend of the Human Torch** (FF #164, ~age 19–20). First voluntary attachment, structurally aligned with the wound.
4. **Girlfriend** → **revealed subject + heir to the powers** (FF #190–191). Revelation moment; defenses pivot from dissociative to identification-with-aggressor in a single arc.
5. **Heir to the powers** → **the second Human Torch** (FF #203 onward). Identity overwritten with boyfriend's; she experiences this as autonomy.
6. **Second Torch** → **Nova, Herald of Galactus** (FF #244, 1982). Patron upgrade to cosmic scale; she experiences this as liberation.
7. **Herald** → **ideological agent of cosmic genocide** (*SS* #50–#75, late 1980s–1992). The role hardens into a worldview; provocation of Surfer is the visible symptom of an internal structure that can no longer afford a single concession.
8. **Agent** → **decapitated body, dispersed** (*SS* #75, 1992). The body she was never granted ownership of is taken from her one last time.
9. **Body** → **symbol, in the memory of the survivor (Surfer) who could not save her** (1992–present). She is curated, posthumously, by a man more powerful than she was, into a meaning he can use. The pattern completes.

Every transition in this sequence is, from the subject's interior viewpoint, an *upgrade* — and every transition is, from a structural viewpoint, the same act performed by a larger and larger figure: someone with more power rewrites her into a more useful version of herself, and she accepts the rewriting as her own decision. The completeness of the pattern is what makes the file legible. It is also what makes the file sad in a way that a competently maintained surveillance archive must, at some point, simply admit.

---

## 4.5 Current Threat Assessment / Status of File

**Active threat:** none. Subject is deceased.

**Conditional threat:** if restored — by Galactus's prerogative, by a cosmic reset, by editorial decision in a future cosmic crossover — the prior pattern is the prior pattern. She would resume Herald duties without psychological reorganization, because the psychological reorganization she would need has never been performed. There is no version of revived-Frankie that is safer than dead-Frankie unless the revival is accompanied by an intervention she has never had access to: a relationship in which she is neither used nor curated, in which her affect can be metabolized rather than escaped, and in which her body is allowed to be hers. Such an intervention is, on the present evidence, beyond the capacity of the figures currently in her orbit.

**Recommended file disposition:** retain as closed-arc reference. Cross-link to Surfer file (load-bearing posthumous), to Galactus file (former herald, terminal outcome), to Storm/Johnny file (former primary attachment, low residual entanglement), to Skrull intelligence cross-reference (war-crime register, hostile read), and to the broader **Herald cohort** comparative file, where her trajectory functions as the negative-space counterpoint to Surfer's: the herald who never resisted, and what that route arrives at.

She is, at the time of this section's compilation, a name spoken occasionally in cosmic contexts, an iconographic flame in a flashback panel, a moral weight in someone else's internal monologue, and otherwise — at last — at rest. Whether rest is what she would have wanted is a question her file does not contain the data to answer, because she was never afforded the conditions under which such a question could be asked of her.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: FRANCES "FRANKIE" RAYE

## Classification: Cumulative Somatic File — Pediatric Iatrogenic Origin → Cosmic-Class Conversion → KIA

---

## 0. Framing Note

The medical record of this subject is unusual in that it cannot be assembled from her own testimony, because for the first two decades of her life she did not know what had been done to her body, and for the last decade of her life her body was no longer organized along human metabolic lines. The dossier must therefore be reconstructed in three discontinuous registers: the **covert pediatric record** (what was done to her in childhood, knowable only retrospectively from the Horton confrontation and from inference); the **overt adult human record** (what was observable to ordinary clinicians and to her own subjective report from approximately ages 5 through ~22); and the **post-conversion record** (Herald-class augmentation, non-human biology, terminal trauma). Each register has its own evidentiary base and its own characteristic gaps.

---

## 1. Antenatal, Neonatal, and Early Childhood (pre-Horton)

No anomalies on record. Biological father deceased or absent prior to subject's earliest continuous memory; biological mother remarried Professor Phineas T. Horton when subject was a young child. Subject presents in all later imagery as a typical Caucasian female of unremarkable build, suggesting an unremarkable developmental baseline. There is no published evidence of congenital condition, birth complication, atypical milestone, or pediatric illness in the years preceding the Horton intervention. Insofar as the woman she became was sculpted, the clay was ordinary.

This matters. It means that every subsequent anomaly in her medical history is *iatrogenic* — produced by intervention, not endogenous — and that the comparison case (who Frankie would have been without Horton) is recoverable in principle: a healthy female human with conventional dermal tolerance, conventional emotional development, and no special relationship to fire.

---

## 2. The Horton Protocol (covert pediatric, approx. ages 5–10)

Reconstructed from *Fantastic Four* #190–191 (Wolfman/Pollard, 1978) and from the somatic and psychological residue observable across the entire adult record. Horton, the engineer of the original android Human Torch (Jim Hammond), used his stepdaughter as a successor experiment — a living, organic test bed for a chemical solution he variously described as "impervium" and which appears to be a derivative of the catalytic chemistry that produced Hammond's plasma combustion shell.

The protocol, as inferred, comprised at minimum three coupled components.

**(a) Repeated dermal/systemic chemical exposure.** The compound was applied to her skin and almost certainly absorbed systemically; the eventual capacity to generate pyroplasmic flame from her own body implies that the agent did not merely coat her but reorganized subcutaneous tissue, vascular structure, and metabolic pathway at the cellular level. This was not a single dose. The thoroughness of the resulting fire-immunity — total, not partial — and the latent capacity for full Torch-equivalent powers strongly suggest a multi-session pediatric exposure across years, with the child unable to consent and almost certainly unable to remember the sessions even contemporaneously, because:

**(b) Concurrent hypnotic / conditioning intervention.** Horton paired the chemical work with a deliberate program of memory suppression. The evidence is conclusive: the adult subject had zero conscious access to the procedures despite their physical magnitude (her entire body had been chemically rewritten), and the suppression broke only on direct confrontation with the perpetrator in adulthood. This is not ordinary childhood amnesia; this is engineered amnesia targeting a specific somatic-procedural memory set while leaving general autobiographical memory of childhood functionally intact. The technique would today be classified somewhere between hypnotic age-regression conditioning and chemically-assisted memory suppression; the precise mechanism is unrecoverable because Horton died at the moment of revelation and left no surviving notes accessible to the FF.

**(c) Somatic / motoric programming.** This is the most unsettling inference and the most secure one. When the adult subject discovered her powers in #190–191, she displayed **no learning curve**. She did not fumble with flight, fail to control flame discharge, or injure herself or bystanders while calibrating output — the entire arc of trial-and-error that even gifted metahumans pass through (compare Johnny Storm's own early FF appearances, or Hammond's century of refinement) was absent. The most parsimonious explanation is that the conditioning included extensive motoric rehearsal — the child was *trained* to use the powers she did not consciously know she had. Her body had run the drills. Only her awareness had been wiped.

**Coupled pyrophobia (the surface symptom).** The conditioning's most visible byproduct was a precisely tuned specific phobia of open flame, sufficient to provoke tachycardia, freezing, panic dissociation, and avoidance of physical intimacy that risked exposing her skin to heat or to the gaze of a partner. The phobia served Horton's experimental control: it kept the subject away from accidental ignition events that might have triggered uncontrolled power expression before he was ready, and it kept her from forming the kind of intimate relationship in which a partner might notice the unusual properties of her skin. The phobia was, in effect, a fence around the laboratory.

**Psychological impact of the Horton Protocol.** Catastrophic and foundational. The subject grew up inhabiting a body that was no longer biologically human while believing it was; experiencing a phobia she could not source; carrying a generalized body-shame ("don't let anyone see," "don't let anyone touch in certain ways") that she experienced as her own personality rather than as an imposed perimeter. Her "self" as constituted in adolescence was already a curated artifact. None of this was available to her conscious awareness until age ~22.

---

## 3. Adolescence and Young Adulthood — the Overt Human Record (approx. ages 11–22)

What an ordinary pediatrician would have seen, had she been seen by one:

- **Vital signs and growth:** unremarkable, within range for a healthy young woman.
- **Skin:** apparently unremarkable on inspection; in fact totally fire-resistant on contact, a property never tested in clinical setting because the phobia ensured she never permitted such testing and never accidentally ignited.
- **Specific phobia, pyrophobic type:** severe, lifelong-presenting, with autonomic correlates (tachycardia, hyperventilation, freezing, dissociation). Triggers: open flame of any size, including matches, candles, a stove burner, and — devastatingly, when she met him — Johnny Storm's transformation. Onset: not recoverable to her; "as long as I can remember." This is the textbook presentation of a phobia with traumatic etiology in a period the patient cannot access — i.e., a phobia with engineered amnesia underneath.
- **Sexual / intimate guarding:** would not allow herself to be seen undressed; would not permit certain forms of touch. She framed this as modesty; the underlying somatic conviction was that her body was wrong, marked, dangerous to expose. Critically, this presented *before* she had any conscious knowledge of why.
- **Dissociative features:** circumscribed amnesia for the Horton sessions, presenting as ordinary "I just don't remember much before age 8 or so." Subjectively unremarkable; objectively profound.
- **No record of:** seizures, syncope, head injury, surgeries, hospitalizations, allergies, chronic medications, eating disorder, self-harm, substance use. The overt record is conspicuously clean. The conditioning was efficient.

**Psychological impact of this period.** She entered adulthood as a high-functioning, conventionally attractive, socially capable young woman whose interiority was organized around a phobia she could not interrogate and an intimacy-guarding she did not understand. She formed a relationship with Johnny Storm in spite of — and, it must be said, plausibly *because of* — his being the human embodiment of her core terror. The proximity to flame she could not tolerate in the abstract she courted in the relational. This is consistent with the unconscious drive of trauma survivors to re-approach the wound.

---

## 4. Acute Revelatory Trauma (*FF* #190–191, ~age 22)

In a single sequence the subject sustained four simultaneous traumatic discoveries: (a) her stepfather had experimented on her in childhood; (b) her body was not biologically what she had believed it to be; (c) her defining phobia was an artifact of conditioning, not a true expression of self; (d) her stepfather then died (killed by Jim Hammond, his original creation) in front of her. The conditioning's hypnotic substrate collapsed; the suppressed somatic memory broke through; the phobia remitted abruptly and totally — a clean, almost suspicious remission, suggesting that the phobia had been actively maintained by the conditioning rather than fading slowly as ordinary phobias do when treated.

**Acute medical presentation:** none documented. No collapse, no syncope, no acute stress reaction requiring intervention. Within the same arc she was demonstrating control of pyroplasmic flame.

**Psychological impact.** This is where the record turns. A person with ordinary psychological resources would have required months to years of integration. The subject required, by published evidence, days. The absence of a grief reaction, the absence of acute dissociative decompensation, the absence of any observed period of withdrawal — all of these are themselves symptoms. She bypassed mourning by *adopting the powers and the role*, effectively short-circuiting the trauma response by collapsing victim and weapon into one identity. The body that had been done-to became the body she did-with.

---

## 5. Second Human Torch Period (~age 22–~age 24)

**Physical capacities:** full Torch-analog: pyroplasmic generation across the surface of the body, controlled discharge, sustained flight via thermal jet, immunity to her own combustion and to ambient flame. No published evidence of injury, overexertion, power-failure, or somatic difficulty in this period. She is operationally indistinguishable from a metahuman who had developed these powers organically.

**Adopted name:** "Frankie Raye, the second Human Torch" — the medical relevance being that she chose, when asked who she was, to identify herself by her boyfriend's hero name rather than by any independent designation. Identity is a somatic fact for a person with no independent self-concept; she literally wore his name on her body in flame.

**Reproductive / endocrine considerations:** unknown but probably altered. The chemical reorganization of her tissues that permitted plasma generation almost certainly affected endocrine function; no record of menstrual history, fertility, or contraception use exists, but the assumption of ordinary human reproductive biology in a body capable of sustaining surface-temperature plasma combustion is implausible. This was never clinically investigated.

**Substance use:** none recorded. Caffeine, alcohol — unremarked. She did not self-medicate in the period when self-medication would have been most expected (the months following the Horton revelation). This is consistent with her overall pattern: she does not soothe; she advances.

**Psychological impact.** The powers functioned as somatic prosthesis for the missing self. As long as she was on fire, she was *someone* — specifically, she was the realized intention of her abuser, but reframed as her own choice. The flight-into-power was, in effect, a continuous mild dissociative state stabilized by exertion. She was happiest in the air. This is significant.

---

## 6. Cosmic Conversion — Galactus's Augmentation (*FF* #244, ~age 24)

A second total bodily transformation, this time undergone with full conscious consent, even eagerness. Galactus, restored by Reed Richards, augmented the subject with the Power Cosmic, converting her into the Herald designated **Nova**.

**Procedural notes (inferred from Herald conversions generally — Radd, Gabriel, Pyreus, Morg, et al.):** Galactus's conversion is not surgical but ontological. The recipient's biological substrate is replaced or overwritten by a cosmic-energy matrix that maintains the body's outward form (in Frankie's case, augmented in scale and silvered/gilded in surface), suspends ordinary metabolic need (no requirement for food, water, oxygen, sleep in conventional senses), and confers FTL flight, stellar-range sensorium, planetary-scale energy manipulation, and durability sufficient to survive cosmic environments.

**Specific augmentation profile (Nova-class):**
- Cosmic flame manipulation at planetary scale (her terrestrial pyroplasmic capacity scaled up by orders of magnitude and recolored from Torch-orange to cosmic-gold).
- FTL flight across interstellar and intergalactic distances.
- Sensory range sufficient to identify and assess inhabited planetary bodies at stellar distances.
- Suspension of human endocrinology — and with it, suspension of the affective registers (anxiety, grief, longing, sexual desire in human form) that had organized her interior life.

**Critical somatic-psychological point.** For Herald subjects with intact human psychology (Radd, Gabriel), the suppression of endocrine-mediated affect is repeatedly shown to be *destabilizing* — they describe a flattening, a loss, a hunger for the lost emotional register. For Frankie, whose human endocrine baseline had been chronically dysregulated by trauma and whose affective life had been organized around dissociation and avoidance, the Power Cosmic suppression was **relieving**. She was, post-conversion, observably *more* serene, more decisive, more present than she had ever been as a human. The augmentation did not impose a foreign calm; it removed a chronic pain. This is medically and ethically important: her contentment as Nova is real, not artifact, but it is the contentment of a person who has finally escaped a body whose tuning she could not bear.

**Psychological impact.** Total. The conversion completed a trajectory begun by Horton: the human body was finally fully replaced. The conversion also fulfilled the unconscious demand of her attachment template — she was now bonded somatically as well as relationally to a devouring parental figure, and the bond was explicit, contractual, and consensual on both sides. For a survivor whose template for love was being-used, Galactus's open instrumentality was the first honest relationship of her life.

---

## 7. Herald-Period Operational Record (~10 years)

No medical incidents on file. She was injured occasionally in conflict (notably in encounters with Skrull defense forces and during her engagements with other Heralds and cosmic actors), but Herald durability and Galactus's capacity to restore his Heralds rendered ordinary injury non-persistent. There is no record of illness — the body class is not subject to illness. There is no record of psychiatric decompensation; the affective flattening of Herald conversion would in any case have masked one if present.

The one consistent **behavioral medical sign** of this period was her selection bias toward inhabited planets. This is, in clinical terms, evidence of moral disengagement scaled to cosmic level; it is also, in somatic terms, evidence that her pyroplasmic instrument had finally been pointed at a target proportionate to the magnitude of what had been done to her — the destruction of worlds by fire, by a woman whose body had been built around fire without her consent. The Skrull genocide selection (*Silver Surfer* #75, Starlin) is the act in which the wound and the weapon are at last fully congruent.

---

## 8. Terminal Event (*Silver Surfer* #75, 1992)

**Cause of death:** decapitation by cosmic energy weapon, wielded by Morg the Executioner, mid-flight in deep space.

**Acute presentation:** instantaneous, no observed period of suffering, no last-words sequence of the kind that would suggest a recoverable interval.

**Post-mortem:** no body recovered in a sense meaningful for a Herald-class entity; her cosmic energy matrix dispersed. She has appeared subsequently in flashback and in brief revivals across Annihilation-adjacent material and FF anniversary appearances, but the operational record closes at *SS* #75.

**Psychological note on the death itself.** She died in service, mid-mission, loyal, undoubting. From the standpoint of her constructed self, this is the optimal outcome — the resolution she had built remained intact to the moment of cessation. She was not given the cracking-open she would have needed to integrate what had been done to her, but she was also spared it. Whether that is mercy or its opposite is not a medical question.

---

## 9. Cumulative Assessment

The medical history is, viewed as a whole, the history of a body **twice rewritten without restoration of the original** — first covertly by Horton, then overtly by Galactus — with a brief intervening period (the Second Torch interval) in which the subject inhabited a hybrid form that retained human relational structure while expressing the products of the first rewriting. The body she died in had no continuous biological line to the body she was born in. The remarkable thing is not that she died at cosmic scale; it is that the woman who died as Nova and the child who was first dosed with impervium in a basement laboratory were related only by name and by the unbroken thread of conditioning that ran between them.

There is no point in this record at which the subject inhabited a body that was wholly her own. The medical history is, finally, the history of that absence.


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — FRANCES "FRANKIE" RAYE

## Classification: Subject File — Bodily Pattern Mapping, Longitudinal (childhood → Herald-class → terminal)

---

## 1. PRELIMINARY NOTE ON THE BODY AS EVIDENCE

The subject's body is the primary archive of her history. More than her speech or her stated beliefs, her musculature, her posture, her gait, the small choreographies of her hands around her own torso — these record what her conscious memory was for two decades not permitted to hold. The Somatic Atlas is therefore in two parts that operate simultaneously: an *implanted somatic vocabulary* (the body trained by Horton beneath awareness — fireproof, combustion-capable, motorically pre-programmed) and a *defensive somatic vocabulary* (the body's own attempts to mark, contain, and protect the territory the conditioning had claimed). The two are not always aligned. Watching her move, pre-revelation, is watching two bodies share a skin: one that *knows* it can hold flame, and one that has been instructed to forget, and has compensated by producing a phobic perimeter around the very capacity it secretly possesses. Post-revelation she resolves the contradiction by ceding to the implanted body. Post-cosmic she ceases to have a body in the human sense at all, and the atlas changes accordingly.

---

## 2. BASELINE ANTHROPOMETRY AND APPEARANCE

Caucasian female, approximate height 5'8", slender athletic build, long red hair worn loose to mid-back in the civilian period and progressively shorter / more sculpted as her identity consolidated into the Torch role. Eye color green. Skin notably *un-freckled* despite the red hair — a small somatic anomaly consistent with the impervium-altered dermis (the chemistry that made her fire-tolerant also appears to have suppressed normal melanin response to UV). She tans poorly and burns not at all; she is not observed to sunburn even in extended outdoor scenes set on beaches and rooftops. Body hair sparse, nails grow slowly — the dermal alteration extends to keratin production. Dental record clean; she has never been observed with the cold-sores, bruises, or minor wounds a normal civilian would accumulate, and on the rare occasions a small abrasion is visible it has healed by the next scene. None of these anomalies are remarked upon by her or by Johnny in the pre-revelation period; she has lived inside this body long enough to consider its quietness normal.

Carriage: tall but not assertive. The shoulders sit slightly forward of the spine's vertical, a protective ribcage-cover that is *not* a slouch — the head stays up and the chin level — but a subtle inward folding of the upper chest. The carriage of a woman who has, since childhood, been quietly armoring her sternum without knowing why.

---

## 3. THE CIVILIAN PERIOD (FF #164–#189): PHOBIC ARCHITECTURE

### 3.1 Gait and locomotion

She walks with a long, even stride, slightly toed-in, hips quiet, arms swinging at low amplitude. She does not bounce. Her footfall is light — the body of someone who has been trained, without knowing it, to move heat-efficiently. On stairs she leads consistently with the right foot and trails the left; on escalators she stands rather than walks. She prefers to walk on the *outside* of a sidewalk pair (curb side), which is unusual for a woman of her cohort and reads as a small territorial assertion that is otherwise absent from her interpersonal repertoire — the body claims space the personality does not.

Notable avoidance pattern: she will adjust her route, mid-stride and without apparent thought, to avoid passing close to open flame. Observable in FF-era scenes near a hot-dog vendor's grill, a restaurant tableside flambé, and a Times Square steam vent (the steam, not flame, still triggers a half-second hesitation — the conditioning over-generalizes to anything atmospherically hot). She does not *notice* she is rerouting. Asked, she would not be able to explain.

### 3.2 Hands and arms

Hands: long-fingered, ungloved by preference, but with a habitual self-touching choreography that functions as a perimeter check. Catalog of recurring hand gestures, civilian period:

- **The collarbone graze:** index and middle fingertips of the right hand drawn lightly along the right clavicle, ending at the sternal notch. Frequency: roughly every four to six minutes in conversation; sharply elevated (every 30–60 seconds) in proximity to heat sources. Function: reassurance that the upper chest — the area Horton presumably first applied the agent — is intact.
- **The wrist-cover:** left hand cupped over the inside of the right wrist, briefly, particularly when greeted or introduced. The wrists are where pulse can be felt; she is checking, beneath conscious awareness, that her body is responding to social stimuli the way she believes it should.
- **The hair-rope:** she gathers her hair into a single rope over the right shoulder and runs it through her left hand. This is partly grooming, partly a way to keep the hair away from the back of her neck — another implanted heat-aware behavior masquerading as a fashion tic.
- **The plate-test:** before eating, she will rest a fingertip on the rim of a plate or the side of a mug. Stated reason, if asked: checking that it isn't too hot. Actual function: confirming her own thermal perception is functioning normally, which (because she is more heat-tolerant than baseline) she has secretly worried about for years.

She does not gesture broadly when she speaks. Hands stay below sternum height. When she laughs she covers her mouth with the back, not the palm, of her hand — a small marker of a woman who learned early to control the visibility of her own affect.

### 3.3 Face and micro-expression

Resting face: pleasant, mouth slightly upturned, brows neutral. She has trained a "social default" that does not require ongoing maintenance — a useful trait in a person whose interior is busier than she lets on. Smile: full, easy, reaches the eyes; this smile is genuine and she deploys it generously. It is also, diagnostically, *too available* — present in moments where a baseline person would show puzzlement or discomfort. The smile is a kind of buffer.

Micro-pattern around flame: a four-stage cascade observable in slow motion across her FF-era appearances.
1. **Pupil dilation** (within ~200ms of flame appearance), inconsistent with the bright ambient light — autonomic, not visual.
2. **Shoulder retraction and breath-hold** (~400ms), upper rib expansion arrested mid-inhalation.
3. **Lip compression**, the smile flattening into a thin straight line — the buffer collapsing.
4. **Withdrawal step or full freeze** depending on flame size; small flames (a match, a stovetop) produce freeze, larger flames (Johnny's transformation) produce a single backward step followed by stillness.

Recovery from these episodes is fast in observable behavior — under ninety seconds to return to social baseline — but the collarbone-graze frequency stays elevated for the rest of the scene.

Eye contact: good, slightly above average duration, but she breaks contact *downward and to her own right*, never upward — a person who looks away by retreating into the body, not by seeking the sky. Post-revelation this reverses.

### 3.4 Intimate / private body behavior

The most diagnostically loaded domain of the civilian period. She will not undress in front of Johnny; she will not let him see her shower; she insists on darkness during sex and on keeping at least some clothing on. She does not state the reasons because she cannot access them. Inferred somatic pattern:

- She bathes alone, with the door locked, in lukewarm water — never hot. Showers are brief and oriented around the *back* of her body; she washes her front with a cloth, eyes averted from her own torso in the mirror.
- She dresses and undresses in a specific sequence that minimizes the time her sternum and upper abdomen are exposed even to herself: she removes a top by pulling the hem up and the new garment down in nearly the same motion. Bras are put on facing-forward and rotated, not reached-behind, because the reach-behind posture briefly extends and exposes the chest.
- Sleepwear: high-necked, long-sleeved, even in summer. She runs slightly cool to the touch (the altered metabolism) and reports being "always a little cold," which is partially true and partially a justification.
- Sexual intimacy: she is responsive, even enthusiastic, *above the clavicle* (kissing, neck, face) and *below the navel*; the central torso is the region she has unconsciously walled off. Johnny, who is twenty-two and not an attentive somatic reader, experiences this as ordinary modesty.

She sleeps on her left side, knees drawn up, right arm across the chest — the same protective arm-bar she carries into her waking posture, made explicit in unconsciousness. Sleep architecture in the civilian period is restless; she wakes 3–5 times a night, briefly, without recalling dreams. Total sleep ~6.5 hours, fragmented.

### 3.5 Eating

Eats quickly, small portions, prefers cool foods — salads, sandwiches, ice cream, iced drinks. Will let coffee cool to lukewarm before drinking. Disclaims a "sweet tooth" that is in fact a *cold-things* preference. Will not eat soup served at temperature. Has never in observed life ordered fondue, hot pot, anything flambéed, anything served in a sizzling skillet. Reads these preferences as personal taste. They are not.

### 3.6 Voice and respiration

Voice: mid-register, warm, with a slight upward inflection at sentence-ends that softens declarative content into something more conversational. Speaks at a moderate pace; does not interrupt. Laugh: easy, unforced, slightly higher in register than her speaking voice. She does not raise her voice. Even in argument with Johnny she modulates downward.

Respiration: shallow upper-chest breathing predominates, ~16–18 breaths per minute at rest (slightly elevated for her age and fitness). Diaphragmatic excursion is limited — the protective inward fold of the upper chest is also the architecture of a person who has not breathed deeply, comfortably, into the bottom of her lungs in many years. Sighing is rare. Yawning is rare. The whole respiratory apparatus is held quietly braced.

---

## 4. THE REVELATION AND TORCH PERIOD (FF #190–#243): RAPID RECONFIGURATION

### 4.1 The acute event

Across the Horton confrontation and its immediate aftermath, the somatic catalog shows a single, sharp inversion. Observable within hours of the revelation:

- The collarbone-graze ceases. Within days the wrist-cover ceases. The hair-rope persists as a now-conscious mannerism.
- She breathes lower in the abdomen for the first time in adult observation; a visibly different ribcage carriage by the end of FF #191.
- The eye-break-downward reverses to an eye-break-*upward* — when she looks away from a conversation now, she looks toward the ceiling or the sky. This is a small thing and a profound one. It signifies a re-orientation of where she locates herself.
- Within two weeks she is sleeping on her back, arms loose at her sides. The protective arm-bar is gone. Total sleep extends to ~7.5 hours, less fragmented.

What does not change: the smile-as-buffer; the moderate vocal modulation; the avoidance of rumination; the absence of solitary processing time. The behaviors that protected her from her *knowledge* dissolve; the behaviors that protected her from her *interior* remain.

### 4.2 New somatic vocabulary as Torch

Once she begins training and operating as the second Human Torch, an entirely new gestural repertoire emerges and consolidates within months — too fast for genuine learning, consistent with the implanted motoric programming surfacing.

- **The flame-ignition trigger:** she opens her hands palms-up, fingers slightly splayed, and exhales sharply through pursed lips at the moment of ignition. The exhalation is not mechanically required; it is a tell. She has unconsciously coupled the new capacity to a breath, the way a singer commits to a note.
- **Mid-flight posture:** body extended, head tilted slightly back, arms forward and parallel — almost worshipful, eyes upward (the same upward gaze that has replaced her downward eye-break on the ground). Where Johnny's flight is acrobatic and play-oriented, hers is *ascensional* — she goes up more than she banks.
- **Power-down recovery:** on landing she shakes her hands twice at the wrist, a small "dispersal" gesture, then runs both palms down her own ribs and hips, smoothing imaginary fabric. The hand-down-the-ribs is the *old* collarbone-graze, displaced lower and outward — the perimeter check has not vanished, it has migrated.
- **Eating shifts:** she begins drinking coffee hot, eating soup, eating spicy food. She mentions discovering she "likes heat now." The behavior reads, correctly, as a body claiming the territory that was previously off-limits.
- **Dress:** lower necklines, shorter sleeves, sleeveless costumes when in the field. She lets Johnny see her. The intimacy avoidance dissolves; her sexual presentation becomes notably more confident and direct.

### 4.3 What persists

The non-rumination. The cheerful surface. The orientation toward the dominant figure in the room (now Reed, when Reed is present, with Johnny remaining the affectional anchor but not the gravitational one). She still does not gesture broadly when speaking. She still does not raise her voice. She still smiles when a baseline person would frown. The body has switched its outer language; the underlying organization is identical.

### 4.4 A small tell that nobody catches

In FF issues across the Torch period, when she is in a room with someone discussing parents, fathers, or family history, she pulls her hair forward over the right shoulder and runs it through her left hand — the old hair-rope — and her speech rate increases by approximately fifteen percent for the next two to three sentences. The conscious mind does not visit the Horton material. The body still does.

---

## 5. THE HERALD PERIOD (FF #244 ONWARD): POST-HUMAN SOMATICS

### 5.1 The conversion event

The Power Cosmic augmentation produces an immediate and total change. The body she leaves Earth in is *not the body she returns in*. Skin reorganized to a cosmic-flame surface (gold, then variegated stellar tones depending on the writer/era); hair replaced with continuous flame; the proportions extended subtly toward the iconic Herald silhouette. More important than the visual: the entire endocrine substrate of the human body is suspended or rewritten. She no longer breathes in the respiratory sense. She no longer requires sleep. She no longer eats. The autonomic small-vocabulary of the civilian period — the pulse-check, the breath-hold, the rib-protection — has nothing to act on anymore. The body has been emptied of the substrate the defenses were defending.

She experiences this, observably, as relief.

### 5.2 New Herald-period gestural vocabulary

- **The standing rest:** she does not sit. Across her appearances as Nova, she is shown standing, hovering, or in flight; almost never seated. When she is "still" she is upright with arms loose at her sides and feet a few inches above whatever surface is beneath her. The body has lost the architecture of fatigue.
- **The reporting posture (before Galactus):** when delivering a planet-find to her patron, she presents with hands at her sides, palms facing slightly forward (an open, surrendered offering of self), chin level, eyes up and direct. This is the posture she could not produce around a human authority figure. She produces it effortlessly here. The submission is not strained because it has been chosen.
- **The flight ignition:** absent in the Herald period. Where Torch-Frankie needed the open-palm exhalation to fire, Nova-Frankie ignites and extinguishes silently and continuously; flame is no longer event, it is medium. The "tell" of the Torch period vanishes because there is nothing to trigger.
- **Hair / flame manipulation:** the old hair-rope reappears in a new form — she is observed, at moments of contemplation or contained pleasure, drawing a tongue of her own flame-hair forward over her right shoulder and letting it spiral through her left hand. The gesture is identical. The substrate has changed. She does not appear to notice she is still doing it.
- **Smile:** persists, modified. Wider, more often, less buffered — the smile of a person who is no longer using it to manage discomfort but who has retained it as a baseline expression. In conversation with Surfer it broadens into something close to a smirk when he raises moral concerns; this is the closest she comes to overt contempt.
- **Eye behavior:** her gaze in the Herald period is *steady and elevated*. The downward-right break is entirely gone. She looks at her interlocutor; when she looks away she looks toward a star.

### 5.3 What persists across the cosmic transition

This is the most diagnostically important section of the entire atlas. The somatic features that survive *every* substrate change — civilian body, Torch body, Herald body — constitute the irreducible core of who she has become.

1. **The hair-through-the-hand gesture**, in all three eras, in three different physical forms.
2. **The orientation toward the most powerful figure in any room**, expressed bodily by foot direction, torso rotation, and gaze; consistent from her civilian deference to Reed, through her Torch-period deference to the senior FF, to her Herald-period orientation toward Galactus that becomes total.
3. **The absence of broad gesture.** Even in cosmic scale, when describing the destruction of a world, her hands stay close to her body. She is a person who never learned to take up space with her hands and never will.
4. **The smile-as-default**, deployed in inappropriate moments — present at the destruction of inhabited worlds, present when Surfer accuses her of cruelty, present in the final panels before Morg kills her.
5. **The flat moderation of voice.** She does not raise her voice as a Herald either. She announces planetary harvests in the same warm mid-register she used to order coffee.

### 5.4 Intimacy, sexuality, sleep — the negative space

She has no intimate partner in the Herald period. She has no observed solitary time that resembles rest. She has no recorded dream content because, presumably, she no longer dreams. The vast architectures of the human body that her conditioning had distorted are simply no longer present to distort. This is the relief the conversion gave her. It is also a way of describing how much of her was given up to obtain it.

---

## 6. STATE-DEPENDENT SHIFTS — CROSS-ERA SUMMARY TABLE (PROSE)

**Calm / baseline.** Civilian: light footfall, collarbone graze every 4–6 minutes, smile-default, shallow upper-chest breathing, eye-break-down-right. Torch: lower abdominal breath, hair-rope occasional, smile-default, eye-break-up. Herald: hovering stillness, hair-flame-through-hand, smile-default, gaze steady on interlocutor or distant star.

**Mild social stress (introduction, mild conflict).** Civilian: wrist-cover, increased blink rate, vocal pitch upward by a half-tone, hair-rope. Torch: hand-down-ribs (the migrated perimeter check), speech rate up ~15%, smile broadens. Herald: speech rate unchanged, smile broadens, slight elevation of hover.

**Heat-stimulus (flame, hot object).** Civilian: full four-stage cascade — pupil dilation, breath-hold, lip compression, freeze or step-back. Recovery 60–90 seconds, perimeter-checks elevated for remainder of scene. Torch: orienting attention toward the flame, hands opening palms-up unconsciously (the ignition primer), pleasurable affect. Herald: no response — she *is* the stimulus.

**Threat to the body.** Civilian: freeze, then flight; never observed to fight back physically. Torch: ignition, decisive flight or counter-attack, no hesitation. Herald: silent flame escalation, postural drop into combat stance with arms slightly forward; she does not vocalize during combat and does not taunt.

**Threat to the worldview** (the rarest and most diagnostic). Civilian: she has no worldview to threaten; presents bewilderment, then deference. Torch: she will leave the room. Herald: smirk; downward modulation of voice into something colder than her baseline warmth; the *one* affect she developed post-cosmically that was not present before — a quiet, contemptuous patience with people who have not made the choices she made. This is what she shows Surfer. It is also what she shows, briefly, in her last conversation with Johnny before her death.

**Intimacy (sexual / affectional).** Civilian: high responsiveness above the clavicle and below the navel; centrally walled-off torso; darkness preferred; clothing partially retained. Torch: full embodied responsiveness, sexual confidence, the wall dissolved. Herald: absent — no intimate behavior recorded. She has converted the energy entirely into devotion.

**Solitude.** Civilian: restless sleep, fragmented, right arm across chest. Torch: relaxed back-sleeping. Herald: she is never observed alone *at rest*; alone she is always in transit, always working, always en route to or from Galactus. Solitude-without-mission is the one state her body never learned to inhabit, in any of its forms.

**Proximity to Galactus.** A category of its own. Hover-height drops; she settles closer to the ground or floor of his chamber. The reporting posture engages: palms slightly forward, eyes up. Speech slows. The smile, for once, mutes — she is too serious in his presence to deploy the buffer. This is the only relationship in her entire life in which she does not need the buffer, because in his presence she is, in the deepest sense available to her, *home* — meaning *named, used, and certain of her role.*

---

## 7. TERMINAL OBSERVATIONS

In the panels preceding her death at Morg's hands, the somatic record is consistent with the entirety of her Herald period: upright posture, steady gaze, the small smile, hands close to the body. She does not raise her voice. She does not, in the half-second visible before the killing blow, produce a freeze, a step-back, or any defensive recoil. The body that learned in childhood to flinch from flame, and that spent twenty years rehearsing the small choreographies of self-protection, has by the end forgotten how to flinch at all. Whether this is integration or attrition is a question the file cannot resolve. It is, in any case, the last entry.


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

## Subject File — Frances "Frankie" Raye / Nova

---

## 1. Foundational Attachment Architecture

The Raye attachment system was built, not grown. This distinction matters at every subsequent level of analysis. Most disorganized attachment in the clinical literature emerges from inconsistent or frightening caregiving across the ordinary developmental timeline — a parent whose warmth and threat are unpredictable, producing a child whose approach-avoidance signals cannot be resolved into a coherent strategy. Frankie's case is structurally similar but etiologically distinct: her primary caregiver, Phineas Horton, was not erratically frightening. He was *consistently warm and consistently exploiting her*, and the exploiting was hidden from her by the very conditioning he was performing. She therefore did not experience the surface-level whiplash of overt disorganized care. She experienced a caregiver who was, on the conscious record, *good* — and a body that registered, beneath that record, that something was profoundly wrong.

The resulting template is unusual: she presents as **securely attached on the surface** (easy warmth, ready trust, capacity for affectionate engagement) while organized at the somatic and structural level around **disorganized** features (a body that braces against intimacy it cannot consciously explain, an inability to be fully seen, a phobic perimeter around the very element that marked her). This split — surface security over structural disorganization — is the master pattern of her relational life. Every relationship she forms reproduces it.

It also explains the most diagnostically peculiar feature of her early-published behavior: she is, by all conscious accounts, a person who *likes people*, who attaches readily, who enjoys her partners, who is sexually present and emotionally available — and yet who at specific somatic flashpoints (undress, exposure to flame, certain modes of being touched) freezes, withdraws, or panics, *without being able to say why*. The split between her conscious relational style and her somatic relational truth is so wide that she lives entirely in the former and treats the latter as an inexplicable malfunction of her own body. This is, of course, exactly what her conditioning was designed to produce.

---

## 2. The Caregiver Template: Horton

The Horton relationship sets every parameter that follows. It must be reconstructed carefully because Frankie herself never reconstructs it; she discovers it whole in *FF* #190–191 and immediately stops examining it.

Horton was not, in her conscious experience, abusive. The conditioning ensured this. He was the stepfather who raised her after her mother remarried, presumably attentive enough that no obvious red flags surfaced; the only signs of damage were the phobia and the somatic guarding, which both she and the adults around her took as her own idiosyncrasy. What she *learned* from him, at the level of implicit relational knowing, were the following propositions:

- **Love and use are the same act.** The hand that fed her also dosed her. There was no separation in her experience between being cared for and being instrumentalized, because the instrumentalization was invisible.
- **Your body is not yours; it is a project belonging to the man who shaped it.** This is the structural lesson her body learned even though her conscious mind never had access to the evidence.
- **The truth of your situation is unavailable to you; you must trust the figure who knows.** Her conditioned amnesia trained her into a relational stance in which the person above her in the hierarchy had knowledge she did not, about herself, and this asymmetry was natural and safe.
- **Compliance produces continuity; resistance produces nothing because there is nothing to resist.** Since she did not know she was being acted upon, she had no occasion to resist, and so never developed the muscle.

These four propositions are the relational grammar she carries into every subsequent bond. She does not know she carries them. They are not beliefs she could articulate. They are the shape of the slot she presents to other people, and powerful people slot into it without effort.

When she discovers the truth, in the laboratory confrontation, she has perhaps ninety seconds of integration time before Horton dies at Hammond's hands. There is no period of mourning, no protracted reckoning, no therapeutic processing. The man who built her template is removed from the board before she can either confront him fully or rework her bond with him. The template is left intact and orphaned, waiting for the next figure to occupy the parental slot.

---

## 3. The Peer-Lover Slot: Johnny Storm

Johnny is, by the structural logic above, an impossible partner — and that is precisely why she chooses him. He is the human-scale embodiment of the element she was conditioned around. To attach to him is to keep the wound active and unresolved while pretending it is merely a quirky romantic irony.

The granular pattern across *FF* #164–192 is consistent and observable. She is publicly affectionate, unguarded in conversation, easy with his social circle (Ben, Alicia, Sue), able to function in his world. She is, however:

- **Selectively non-physical in specific registers.** She tolerates kissing, hand-holding, public closeness; she will not be undressed in his presence, will not let him see her body in unguarded states, withdraws from forms of contact that approach the conditioned somatic perimeter. She rationalizes this variously — modesty, religious framing in some early dialogue, simply "not yet" — but the rationalization shifts while the underlying refusal is stable. The instability of the explanation across the explainable stability of the behavior is a tell: the behavior is doing work she cannot see.
- **Asymmetrically invested.** Johnny is, by his own behavior in the same period, in love with her in a recognizable adolescent-romantic register: thinking about her when she isn't there, planning around her, mourning her absences. She is fond of him, present with him, but her investment lacks the same forward-leaning gravity. She is *with* him; he is *toward* her.
- **Easily redirected by larger figures.** When Reed enters a room, when Sue speaks, when authority of any kind surfaces, her attention re-centers there. She is polite about it but consistent. Johnny commands her affection but not her orienting reflex.

After the revelation and her acquisition of powers, the relationship reformats but the asymmetry persists. She becomes the "second Human Torch" — taking *his* hero name, training under *his* tutelage, presenting publicly as his counterpart. This looks, superficially, like deepening commitment. Structurally it is the Horton template re-emerging: she allows the man closest to her to author her identity. Johnny does not realize he is being cast as Horton's successor because he is not consciously casting himself that way; he just experiences her as eager to share his world, his name, his powers. From her side it is fluent and easy because it is the only template she has.

Critically, the relationship contains no observed period of **conflict-and-repair**. They do not fight and reconcile. They do not test the bond. There is no scene in which Johnny does something wrong and she demands a change, no scene in which she does something wrong and rebuilds his trust. The bond runs on surface harmony, which means it has no measured tensile strength. When the larger patron appears, it gives way without a crack because it has never been pressure-tested.

The departure in *FF* #244 — her volunteering for the Herald role, leaving Johnny weeping and disbelieving on the ground beneath her — is, from Johnny's side, a catastrophic betrayal. From hers, it is barely a transition. She does not understand why he is so distressed. Her affect in the scene is composed, almost light. This is not coldness. It is the structural truth of the bond: she was *fond of him*, she was *with him*, but she was never *anchored to him* in a way that would make leaving cost her. Anchors require depth. Her depth had nowhere to land in a peer.

---

## 4. The Patron Slot: Galactus

The Galactus bond is the master event of her relational life because it is the first time the slot Horton built finds a figure adequate to fill it. Every previous attachment was a misfit — Horton was too small (a man), Johnny was too peer-level (a boyfriend). Galactus is the correct scale. He is parentally vast, openly instrumental, *explicit* about the terms of the relationship in a way Horton never was. And — this is the part she experiences as liberation — he asks her consent.

The consent is structurally hollow (a person cannot meaningfully consent to becoming an avatar of a world-eater when consent itself is the only act of authorship she has ever been permitted), but she does not experience it as hollow. She experiences it as the first time in her life that a powerful figure has *told her what he wanted from her* and *let her say yes*. To her, this is the corrective experience. Horton hid his use of her; Galactus declares his. By the warped grammar of her template, the declaration *is* love — the first honest version of love she has encountered.

The relational pattern that follows is **devotional** in the technical religious sense:

- **Idealization is total and unwavering.** She does not, across the entire Nova period, voice a single private doubt about Galactus on the page. There are no overheard scenes of her wondering, no flickers of conscience that she suppresses. The idealization is not effortful; it is structural.
- **Service is experienced as joy, not burden.** She seeks out worlds for him with apparent enthusiasm. When she finds a populated planet, she does not flinch; she reports it like a child bringing a parent a good grade.
- **His preferences override her perception.** When the moral content of her work would, in any baseline human, generate distress, she does not feel it. The Power Cosmic plausibly suppresses some of this, but the suppression is operating on a psyche that was already organized to subordinate its own perception to a patron's needs. The augmentation merely closes a loop that was already mostly closed.
- **She has no peer relationship within the bond.** Galactus does not converse with her as an equal; she does not expect or want him to. The asymmetry is the comfort. A peer would require her to have a self; a patron does not.

The bond contains no observed conflict either, and again this is diagnostic. A healthy attachment, even a hierarchical one, generates friction. She generates none with Galactus across years of service. This is not because Galactus is easy to please — the Surfer demonstrably found him exhausting — but because she is constitutionally incapable of registering the friction that would arise. Where Norrin Radd's autonomous moral center scraped against the work, hers had never been built, so the work passed through her without resistance.

---

## 5. The Peer-Rival Slot: The Silver Surfer

Norrin Radd is the most psychologically informative relationship in her file because he is the one she cannot resolve. He occupies a slot her template has no script for: a peer of comparable cosmic stature, formerly bonded to her patron, who has *left* the bond on moral grounds and survived. Everything he is, by his existence, indicts everything she is.

Her treatment of him is correspondingly unstable in a way nothing else in her relational pattern is. She is **contemptuous** of him — calls his moral hesitation weakness, mocks his anguish, frames his conscience as a failure of nerve. The contempt is too loud. She does not treat other figures she dismisses with this volume; she treats them with indifference. The volume of her contempt for the Surfer is the measure of how much he threatens her.

Specifically, he threatens her by:

- **Existing as proof that the Herald role is morally optional.** If he could leave, she could have. The fact that she did not becomes a *choice* rather than a *necessity*, and choices are accountable.
- **Modeling the unprocessed grief she has not done.** He carries the weight of every world he led Galactus to. She carries none. In any honest accounting one of them is malfunctioning; her structure cannot afford for it to be her.
- **Refusing to be wholly dismissible.** She can write off Skrulls as monsters. She cannot write off Norrin Radd, who is plainly noble by any axis she can muster. He is a peer she cannot devalue, and her template has no script for non-devalued peers.

The pattern with him, accordingly, is **derision deployed as defense**, escalating when he presses. She does not soften with him over time; she hardens. This is the only relationship in her file where she shows what looks like genuine, sustained negative affect. It is the closest she comes to feeling the thing she is otherwise organized not to feel. He is, in a real sense, her unintegrated conscience walking around outside her, and her response to that is to attack the projection so the original stays buried.

---

## 6. Absent Slots: Female Peers, Mutual Friendships, Mentors-of-Conscience

The dossier should note what is **not** in her relational file, because the absences are as patterned as the presences.

- **No close female friendships.** She is amicable with Sue, Alicia, Crystal in her FF period, but there are no scenes of confidence, no late-night conversations, no sense of any of these women as someone she would call when something was wrong. The women around her are figures in her boyfriend's life whom she is courteous toward.
- **No mutual peer bonds of any kind.** She has no Ben Grimm in her life — no person of equivalent status with whom she has a horizontal, banter-laden, mutually-corrective friendship. Every relationship in her file is vertical (Horton-above, Galactus-above) or romantic-asymmetric (Johnny-toward).
- **No mentor figure who is benign and non-instrumental.** She has never had, in the published record, a Reed-to-Johnny or Charles-to-Jean figure — an older person who took an interest in her flourishing without wanting to *use* the flourishing for something. The closest available figure, Reed, she relates to with deference but not closeness.
- **No therapeutic figure of any kind.** There is no Doc Samson scene. No reflective interlocutor. She has, across her published life, never sat down with anyone whose job or instinct was to ask her what she was feeling and wait for the answer.

The total absence of horizontal, non-instrumental, conscience-bearing relationships in her life is the negative-space portrait of why she ends up where she ends up. No one was ever in the position to interrupt the trajectory because the trajectory ran through slots that did not include interrupters.

---

## 7. Bonding Mechanics

How she bonds, in observable behavioral terms:

- **Rapid initial warmth.** She does not have an extended testing period with new figures. She arrives present, available, easy. This was likely adaptive in childhood — a child whose situation depends on being a low-friction object of care will develop fluent surface charm.
- **Orientation reflex.** Within minutes of being in a new environment, she has identified the dominant figure and is subtly oriented toward them. Body angle, eye-tracking, conversational deference. She is not sycophantic; the orientation is too automatic for sycophancy. It is a postural default.
- **Adoption of the patron's frame.** Whatever the dominant figure values, she rapidly values. Johnny values heroics; she becomes a hero. Galactus values worlds; she finds worlds. There is no friction or negotiation in the adoption — she experiences the patron's frame as the natural frame.
- **Suppression of her own preferences below the patron's.** Not by struggle; by absence. She does not appear to have strong preferences of her own outside the patron-supplied frame. Asked what *she* wants, in scenes where the question is implicit, she has nothing to offer that is not derived from the active bond.

## 8. Distrust Mechanics

How she registers and processes distrust:

- **Distrust of equals: low to nonexistent.** She does not appear to scan peers for threat or deception. This is consistent with a template in which peers are not relevant figures.
- **Distrust of superiors: structurally impossible.** The Horton conditioning trained her into a default in which the figure above her knows more than she does about her own situation, and this is safe. She cannot generate suspicion toward Galactus because the slot does not contain suspicion. When Surfer attempts to seed it — telling her, in essence, *this is wrong, your patron is wrong* — she experiences his speech as an attack on her, not as information about Galactus.
- **Distrust as defense against doubt.** Where she *does* deploy distrust, it is downward — toward populations she selects for destruction. The Skrulls become "monsters" specifically so that she does not have to trust them as moral subjects. This is distrust functioning as moral pre-emption: by deciding in advance that the targets are untrustworthy, she avoids ever having to weigh their claims.

## 9. Betrayal Mechanics

- **Being betrayed: she does not consciously experience it.** The largest betrayal of her life — Horton's lifelong experiment on her — produces, in her observable behavior, no betrayal-response. She does not rage at his memory, does not curse him, does not refuse his legacy. She continues his work by becoming what he built. This is not forgiveness; it is the absence of the affective machinery that would produce a betrayal-response in the first place.
- **Committing betrayal: she does not register it as such.** Leaving Johnny in *FF* #244 is, by any external moral accounting, a betrayal of an established intimate bond. She does not frame it that way. She frames it as a choice freely made on her own behalf, and Johnny's grief is, to her, a regrettable consequence she did not intend and cannot really process. There is no scene of her later looking back on the departure with regret. She does not appear, in any observed moment, to think of him at all after she leaves.
- **The Surfer-betrayal pattern.** Norrin Radd betrayed Galactus, in her frame, by leaving. She holds this against him in a way she does not hold anything against anyone. This is the one register in which betrayal *registers* for her — when it is committed against her patron. Her own conscience is delegated to him; betrayals of him are felt as betrayals of her.

## 10. Repair Mechanics

The file contains, across her entire published life, **no observed repair sequence**. There is no scene of a relationship that ruptures and is rebuilt. The bonds in her file either run on uninterrupted surface harmony (Johnny pre-departure, Galactus throughout) or fail catastrophically and are abandoned (Johnny post-departure, never reconciled; Horton, dead before reckoning; Surfer, never moved from contempt to dialogue). She does not appear to possess a repair capacity. This is consistent with the template: a person who has never been allowed to register injury cannot develop the muscle for repair, because repair requires first acknowledging injury, then negotiating a restored bond between two parties who can meet as injured peers. None of her bonds have ever permitted that meeting.

---

## 11. Intimacy and Dependency

Intimacy, properly understood, requires the capacity to be *seen* — to allow another person access to one's interior states without managing the access. Frankie does not have this capacity, and the lack predates any of her conscious choices. Horton's conditioning produced a body and a self that *could not be seen*, somatically and structurally. The early pattern with Johnny — refusing to let him see her undressed, withdrawing from contact that would expose her — is the literal expression of this. Even after the conditioning is broken, the structural inability remains.

Her observable intimacies are therefore all forms of **fluent presence without disclosure**. She is *there*, she is *warm*, she is *responsive* — and she is not, in any scene on record, revealing an interior state that the partner did not already have access to from the outside. There is no moment of "let me tell you what I really feel about this." There is no confession, no wound-sharing, no the-thing-I've-never-told-anyone. With Johnny this passes as ordinary romance because they are young and the relationship is new. With Galactus it is the structural form of the bond.

Dependency is similarly inverted. In the ordinary register, dependency is the gradual loaning-out of one's autonomy to a trusted other, with the capacity to call it back. Frankie does not loan; she **transfers**. With each patron, she does not retain a sovereign core that is choosing to depend; she relocates her center of gravity wholly into the patron's frame. This is why each transition (Horton → Johnny → Galactus) is so easy for her: she is not relocating a self from one host to another; she is reassigning a vacancy.

This is also why her dependency does not present, on the surface, as *needy*. Needy dependency is what happens when a partial self leans on another and is anxious about the lean. Total dependency, paradoxically, presents as serene independence — because there is no sovereign self left to feel the anxiety of leaning. She appears confident, choosing, free, because the part of her that would have felt unfree has been outsourced.

---

## 12. The Master Template, Stated Plainly

Across every relationship in her published life, the same shape appears:

1. **A powerful figure occupies the upper slot.** Horton, then Johnny (in the role of identity-author, even though he is not her elder), then Galactus.
2. **She presents an easy, warm, low-friction surface to that figure.**
3. **She allows the figure to author some increment of her identity** — her body (Horton), her name and role (Johnny), her cosmic function and moral universe (Galactus).
4. **She experiences the authoring as liberation rather than imposition,** because the alternative (no author) would expose the vacancy underneath.
5. **She does not pressure-test the bond,** because the bond is structurally too important to risk and because she lacks the repair capacity that would let her survive a rupture.
6. **When a larger figure appears, she transitions** — without conflict, without observable mourning of the prior bond, with affect that suggests the prior bond was never as deep as the partner believed.
7. **Peer relationships do not register meaningfully**; the slot is empty by design.
8. **Conscience-bearing peers (Surfer) provoke her only sustained negative affect,** because they expose the structure and she cannot integrate the exposure.

This template is fully formed before she meets Johnny, fully active throughout her FF tenure, and fully fulfilled in the Herald bond. She did not become this through choice or drift. She was built this way, in a Long Island laboratory, by a man who needed a successful experimental subject and produced, instead of a person, a slot — which the universe then filled with progressively larger figures until the slot found the largest figure available, and she went, smiling, into the fire she had been afraid of all her life.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

## Subject: Frances "Frankie" Raye / NOVA (Herald-Class)

---

## 6.0 Orienting Frame

Frankie Raye's defensive architecture is unusually legible because it was *built* in two distinct construction phases by two distinct architects. The first phase — childhood through age ~20 — was installed *for* her by Phineas T. Horton: a hypnotic-amnesiac scaffold she did not author and could not access. The second phase — from *FF* #191 onward — was assembled *by* her, at speed, atop the rubble of the first, using whatever materials were closest to hand (Johnny, then Galactus). The second architecture's job was to make the first architecture's collapse survivable. It does that job. It does it at catastrophic moral cost.

What follows is the full taxonomy, ranked from the most primitive (Vaillant Level I, "psychotic") through immature, neurotic, and mature defenses, with the positive compensations bracketed at the end. Each entry is anchored to observable behavior across the published record.

---

## 6.1 PRIMITIVE / PSYCHOTIC-LEVEL DEFENSES (Vaillant I)

### 6.1.1 Denial (psychotic-grade, pre-revelation)

For ~20 years Frankie lived in flat denial that anything about her body was unusual, despite extensive somatic evidence to the contrary: the inexplicable pyrophobia, the refusal to be undressed even in trusted intimacy (FF #164–#179), the inability to articulate *why* any of this was so. The denial was not a chosen suppression — it was a structural impossibility of access, installed by Horton's conditioning. It operated by collapsing the question itself: she did not *suppress* the answer, she could not formulate the question. This is the most primitive form of denial because it forecloses the possibility of inquiry rather than the content of an inquiry.

**Behavioral signature:** when Johnny or friends asked about the phobia, she would deflect with bright-tone non-answers, change subject, or — under pressure — display the panic itself, which functioned as a closing of the conversational frame. Observers were taught to stop asking.

### 6.1.2 Distortion (Herald period)

Post-Nova, Frankie reshapes external reality to fit internal need. The Skrulls are not a civilization to her; they are "monsters." Galactus is not a devourer of worlds; he is a cosmic necessity whose service confers grace. The Surfer is not a moral peer raising legitimate objections; he is a weakling clinging to obsolete attachments. None of these reframings are negotiated with evidence — they are imposed on the data so the data stop generating distress. This is distortion in the Kernbergian sense: a *gross* reshaping of reality, not a slight tilt.

---

## 6.2 IMMATURE DEFENSES (Vaillant II)

### 6.2.1 Splitting (her dominant Herald-period defense)

Splitting is the engine of Nova-Frankie. The moral universe bifurcates cleanly:

- **Sacred:** Galactus, his hunger, his survival, his needs.
- **Disposable:** every inhabited world that satisfies that hunger.

There is no middle category. There are no inhabited worlds whose loss she mourns *and* whose destruction she enables — she does not occupy the Surfer's tortured both/and. The split is total and is what allows her to function. When the Surfer attempts to introduce ambivalence — to say *and* rather than *or* — she responds with derision (SS #75 sequence), because ambivalence would re-couple the categories and re-introduce the very pain the split exists to prevent.

She also splits *people*: Horton was wholly father before the revelation, wholly betrayer after; Johnny is wholly beloved during the FF years, wholly secondary the moment Galactus appears; Galactus is wholly luminous from the moment of conversion onward. There is no middle frame in which a person is reckoned with as mixed.

### 6.2.2 Identification with the Aggressor (her *signature* defense)

Anna Freud's classic mechanism: the abused child neutralizes the unbearable position of victim by becoming the abuser, or by becoming the abuser's successful product. Frankie executes both forms.

- **Becoming Horton's product:** within issues of his exposure, she adopts the Human Torch identity — i.e., she completes the experiment Horton ran on her and presents the completion as her own choice. The conditioning becomes a "gift." The violation becomes a "head start."
- **Becoming Galactus's instrument:** she does not merely serve him; she takes pleasure in the selection of victim worlds (SS run). She moves from the position of having-been-marked to that of marking-others. The childhood pattern is preserved at the role level and inverted at the agency level: she is no longer the one to whom something is done.

This defense is what scales her wound to cosmic harm. Without it she would not be Nova; she would be a survivor of unusual childhood abuse who could not sleep at night. With it, she sleeps fine (in whatever sense Heralds sleep), at the cost of populated star systems.

### 6.2.3 Projection (selective, defensive)

She projects her own historical weakness — phobic, panicked, body-alienated, helpless — onto the Surfer, recasting his moral seriousness as squeamishness, his hesitation as cowardice, his grief as sentimentality. This is precision projection: she takes the affective register she has banished from herself and locates it in the only figure in her cosmic peer group who could plausibly carry it. Doing so accomplishes two things: it externalizes the disowned affect, and it permits her to attack it from a position of strength rather than re-encounter it within.

### 6.2.4 Acting Out

Her decision to volunteer as Herald (FF #244) is the clearest acting-out in the file: rather than process the multi-layered trauma of the Horton revelation, the asymmetry with Johnny, the discomfort of being a second-Torch shadow-figure, and the unresolved grief of her stolen childhood, she *acts* — taking an irreversible, life-rewriting step that bypasses all affective work. Heralding is not the cause of her unresolved material; it is the *avoidance* of it, executed at the largest scale available.

Similarly, every Skrull-throneworld-grade decision is an acting-out: when worldview-pressure mounts (Surfer's reproaches), she does not reflect — she escalates the very behavior under critique, choosing a target whose destruction definitively forecloses the conversation.

### 6.2.5 Somatization (pre-revelation only)

Before the conditioning was named, all her conflict ran through the body: tachycardia at flame, freezing when touched too warmly, dissociative withdrawal during intimacy, body-shame around undress. The mind was sealed; the body leaked. This is textbook conversion-pattern somatization, and it ceased the moment the somatic memory was made cognitively available in *FF* #190–#191. The flame phobia did not gradually remit — it dropped, because the conduit of expression was no longer needed.

### 6.2.6 Passive-Aggression (rare, residual)

Largely absent in her presentation, with one structural exception: her *manner* of leaving Johnny in #244. She does not fight with him, does not negotiate, does not even fully argue. She simply chooses Galactus in front of him and goes. The "calm" is a passive-aggressive act in form — a refusal to engage with the relational fact that she is detonating his life — even as it presents as serene. The serenity is the weapon.

### 6.2.7 Fantasy (Schizoid-type)

She has a recurring private narrative — never spoken aloud, but reconstructable from her behavior — in which her life is a *chosen ascent*: from Horton's daughter, to the Torch's girlfriend, to the second Torch, to Herald, to cosmic intimate of the universe's most powerful being. This is a fantasy precisely because the actual record describes a series of curations performed *on* her by men with more power. The fantasy reframes curation as ascent. She lives inside it.

---

## 6.3 NEUROTIC DEFENSES (Vaillant III)

### 6.3.1 Reaction Formation (powerful and stable)
