The thing she most feared becomes the thing she most embraces. Fire — the source of lifelong panic — becomes her name, her body, her job, her cosmic medium. Being-used — the wound of her childhood — becomes her vocation. Cosmic devouring — which on any human moral register is monstrous — becomes the sacred work she defends from criticism. Reaction formation in Frankie is not subtle; it is total, and its totality is itself diagnostic. Real ambivalence produces hedged affect; her affect is unhedged, which is the giveaway.

### 6.3.2 Idealization

Galactus is not merely her patron; he is *idealized* into a being whose needs constitute their own moral category. She speaks of him with awe; she serves with devotion; she registers no flaw. The Surfer's millennia of devotion-then-rebellion she does not learn from. Idealization closes the assessment loop — there is nothing to evaluate because the evaluated object is already perfect.

Note: she also idealized Horton, retrospectively, by the speed with which she forgave the conditioning by reframing it as preparation. The capacity to idealize a documented abuser within issues of confronting him is unusual and predicts the speed with which she idealizes Galactus.

### 6.3.3 Devaluation (the inverse face of idealization)

What she does not idealize, she devalues: her old human life, her relationship with Johnny in retrospect ("small," "constraining," "earthbound"), the Surfer's ethics, the inhabitants of target worlds. Devaluation lets her leave Earth without grief and slaughter civilizations without remorse — both are operations on objects she has already pre-emptively diminished.

### 6.3.4 Intellectualization (light, Herald-period)

When pressed on the ethics of Heralding, she produces *reasoning*: Galactus is necessary, the universe requires balance, Skrulls are monsters, individual lives are bounded against cosmic scale. The reasoning is real-sounding and functions to keep affect at arm's length. She does not feel the worlds end; she categorizes them.

### 6.3.5 Rationalization

Adjacent to but distinct from intellectualization: post-hoc justification of pre-committed choices. She chose Heralding for affective reasons (escape, fusion, mastery of her marked element); she explains it in terms of duty, opportunity, and cosmic significance. The explanation is sincere — she believes it — but it follows the decision rather than producing it.

### 6.3.6 Displacement

Her contempt for the Surfer is plausibly displaced contempt for her *own* pre-Nova self — the hesitant, body-alienated, morally-unsettled human she used to be. She cannot attack that self directly without re-opening the architecture; she attacks its avatar in him instead.

### 6.3.7 Repression (post-revelation, voluntary)

Where pre-revelation amnesia was *imposed* on her, post-revelation she actively *keeps* certain content out of awareness: the grief of her stolen childhood, the question of who she would have been without Horton, any honest reckoning with the human cost of her work. There is no recorded scene in the published canon of Frankie alone with this material. The repression is structural to the post-revelation personality — without it, the personality would not cohere.

---

## 6.4 MATURE DEFENSES (Vaillant IV) — Underdeveloped but Not Absent

### 6.4.1 Sublimation (limited, partial)

The clearest mature defense in her file is the *partial* sublimation of her relationship to fire: from somatic terror, to controlled superhero pyroplasm, to cosmic creative-destructive medium. There is real channeling here, not merely reaction formation — she develops genuine skill and elegance with the element. The trouble is that the sublimation never extends to the *ethical* substrate; she sublimates the medium but not the meaning.

### 6.4.2 Suppression (occasional, mission-tactical)

She can hold affect aside in order to act under pressure — useful in combat, in cosmic logistics, in handling Galactus's demands. This is healthy in form. It coexists with the unhealthy repression of identity-level material.

### 6.4.3 Humor — Absent

The published record contains essentially no instance of Frankie deploying humor as a defense against discomfort. This is itself diagnostic. A subject this defended without humor is a subject whose defenses do not include the metabolizing-of-pain through play. Everything must be either embraced as sacred or rejected as beneath notice.

### 6.4.4 Altruism — Absent in the mature sense

She is loyal, courageous, capable of self-sacrifice — but only within the frame of devotion to a chosen patron. There is no recorded act of altruism that does not flow through, or serve, an attachment figure. The form looks altruistic; the structure is dependent.

### 6.4.5 Anticipation — Functional, narrow

She anticipates well within mission scope (target selection, threat assessment, cosmic navigation). She does *not* anticipate the long-term internal cost of her resolutions, because anticipating it would require introspection she cannot afford.

---

## 6.5 POSITIVE COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

These are real and must be entered into the record without irony. They coexist with the foregoing.

1. **Genuine courage.** Volunteering for Herald-conversion required nerve no human had previously shown in canon for that role. Whatever its motivational substrate, the act itself was brave.
2. **Decisiveness under existential pressure.** She does not freeze, oscillate, or break. The very rigidity that prevents reflection enables performance.
3. **Capacity for loyalty.** Once bonded, she is reliable to the extreme. Galactus loses her only to Morg's blade, never to wavering.
4. **Functional cheerfulness.** Whether defensive or not, her warmth in the human-era issues is real to those around her; she is liked, she lifts mood, she does not corrode rooms.
5. **High pain tolerance, somatic and psychological.** She metabolizes the Horton revelation in days. Most subjects would not metabolize it in years.
6. **Skill acquisition speed.** She masters Torch-class powers without a recorded training arc and adapts to Power-Cosmic-class augmentation without observable difficulty.
7. **Sexual and relational ease (Torch period).** Once the somatic block lifts, she presents as confident, present, embodied — the recovery is unusually clean.
8. **Capacity for sustained mission focus across cosmic time-spans.** Most converted Heralds drift, doubt, defect. She holds.

These positive capacities are not separable from the pathological structure — they are partially the *yield* of it. The same rigidity that prevents introspection enables the courage and the focus. One does not remove the wound without removing the gifts the wound produced.

---

## 6.6 NEGATIVE COMPENSATIONS (full list)

1. **Moral disengagement at planetary and civilizational scale.**
2. **Pleasure in destruction**, particularly in selecting populated targets — the inversion of her own childhood victimhood at cosmic scale.
3. **Pre-emptive devaluation** of any species or culture she is asked to feed to Galactus, with strong preference for re-coding them as "monsters."
4. **Contempt for moral hesitation in peers**, especially the Surfer — a contempt that is louder than the threat warrants, because the peer is a mirror.
5. **Serial role-replacement of self with identities supplied by men**: Horton's subject → Johnny's girlfriend → second Human Torch → Galactus's Nova. Each transition presented as ascent.
6. **Tolerance of instrumentalization as the default condition of love.** She cannot recognize a relationship in which she is not being used by a larger figure; such relationships read as empty.
7. **Incapacity for solitude without mission.** No observed scene of her at rest, unscheduled, without role.
8. **Foreclosure of grief.** Horton, Johnny, her own childhood — none mourned on record.
9. **Brittleness disguised as serenity.** The structure cannot tolerate a single sustained question. The serenity is what a load-bearing wall looks like before it doesn't.

---

## 6.7 Defensive Architecture in Cross-Section

If one were to draw her psyche at the Herald-period peak, the load-bearing elements would arrange as follows, from foundation upward:

- **Foundation:** disorganized attachment (Horton) — un-renovated.
- **Floor:** dissociative amnesia, now decommissioned but leaving a hollow.
- **Walls:** identification with the aggressor + splitting + idealization of patron.
- **Roof:** reaction formation (fire = self; being-used = vocation).
- **Furnishings:** intellectualization, rationalization, devaluation, projection at the Surfer.
- **Windows:** sublimation of the fire-medium, suppression in tactical contexts. (Small windows.)
- **Doors:** none. No mature defenses provide egress from the structure into ordinary human life. This is by design — she does not want to leave.

The architecture is *stable* — that is its most striking property. Most defensive structures this primitive at the immature-level base oscillate, decompensate, leak. Hers does not, because Galactus is a uniquely stabilizing attachment figure: he is always there, always needs her, always confirms the terms. The cosmic patron functions as a structural buttress that no human relationship could have supplied. This is why she found peace at his side and could not have found it anywhere else.

---

## 6.8 What Would Crack It

For completeness, the file notes the conditions under which the architecture would fail:

1. **Loss of Galactus** (not loss of *her* — loss of *him*) — would remove the buttress and force re-encounter with all suspended material.
2. **A sustained, non-dismissible relational mirror** — not the Surfer's intermittent reproach, but extended close contact with a peer she could neither idealize nor devalue.
3. **Re-confrontation with Horton material in a setting she cannot exit by acting out** — i.e., reflective conditions she cannot weaponize into a mission.
4. **A target world she cannot pre-emptively devalue** — one whose inhabitants she is forced to know individually before they are consumed.

None of these conditions obtained in life. She died, by Morg's blade, with the architecture fully intact. That is — by the architecture's own terms — a successful life.

It is the function of this file to note that, by other terms, it was not.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# SECTION 6 — LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE

## Frances "Frankie" Raye / NOVA

> *Methodological note.* What follows tracks the subject across five discrete developmental windows: (a) the pre-conditioning childhood we can only infer; (b) the conditioned-childhood and adolescent period under Horton; (c) the late-adolescent / young-adult "civilian" window (FF #164–#189); (d) the Torch-II window (#190–#243); and (e) the Herald window (#244 through *SS* #75). Each phase is broken out across the three axes requested — affect regulation, cognitive style, self-concept — with the developmental hinge that carries each axis into the next phase named explicitly. All inferences are anchored to published behavior.

---

## Phase I — Pre-Conditioning Infancy and Early Childhood (inferred, pre-Horton-as-stepfather)

We have no direct scenes from this window, but the structure of Phase II requires that a Phase I existed: the conditioning *replaces* a self that briefly existed before it. The subject was born to a mother who later remarried Phineas Horton; there was therefore some interval in which she existed as an ordinary infant/child with an ordinary nervous system, before the impervium regimen and the hypnotic blocks began.

- **Affect regulation:** presumptively normal-range infantile; the later capacity for warm social presentation (her ease with Johnny's circle, the unforced sociability of the FF #164–#180 scenes) suggests an early attachment that was not catastrophic. Something was built before it was overwritten — she is not a *cold* person.
- **Cognitive style:** unknowable, but the adult subject's high baseline competence, quick action-orientation, and capacity for abstraction suggest no pre-existing developmental disorder. She is, by every later measure, a bright child who became a bright adult.
- **Self-concept:** in formation, then *interrupted*. This is the phase whose absence haunts everything after.

**Hinge into Phase II:** the mother's remarriage and the beginning of Horton's access to the child as both parent and experimental subject.

---

## Phase II — Conditioned Childhood and Adolescence under Horton (approx. ages ~4 to ~19)

This is the formative window and the entire later structure rests on it. Horton performs two simultaneous operations: (1) chemical alteration of her body via the impervium derivative, and (2) hypnotic conditioning to suppress conscious memory of (1). The result is a child raised inside an engineered dissociation.

- **Affect regulation.** Bifurcated from the start. On the social surface she develops what appears to have been functional adolescent affect — she emerges from this period able to date, attend Empire State University, befriend Johnny Storm and his sister, hold conversation, flirt, and pass as ordinary. Beneath the surface, a discrete affective channel — anything that activates the suppressed memory — produces immediate, ungovernable panic. The channel is narrow (specifically: flame, exposure of the body, intimate touch that risks disclosure) but absolute within its bandwidth. This is the architecture of a *split* regulator: ordinary affect runs through one circuit, conditioned affect through another, with no integration between them. The subject cannot regulate the second circuit because she cannot consciously access it.
- **Cognitive style.** Forms around the absence. Because there is a domain she cannot think about, she develops a cognitive style that *does not probe* — that handles unbearable material by routing around it rather than into it. This is the origin of the lifelong action-orientation and low introspection later observed. A child who has been hypnotically conditioned to *not look* at part of her own history grows into an adult who does not look at any part of her history. The avoidance generalizes from the specific blocked content to introspection as a habit.
- **Self-concept.** Compromised at root. She experiences herself as the daughter of Phineas Horton, as ordinary, as biologically baseline — and every one of those propositions is false. The self-concept she carries through adolescence is a *fiction maintained by another person*. Crucially, she has no internal sense that anything is wrong at the propositional level; the wrongness leaks through only somatically (the phobia, the body-shame, the refusal to be seen). This produces the lifelong pattern of *believing her own performed self* while her body keeps a separate set of books.

**Hinge into Phase III:** physical separation from Horton (college, dating Johnny) without the conditioning yet broken — the subject leaves the lab but carries the lab inside her.

---

## Phase III — The "Civilian" Window: FF #164 through #189 (early 20s)

This is the window in which she is most legible as a recognizable clinical case before everything detonates. The subject is functional, attractive, socially integrated, in a serious relationship — and showing florid symptoms of dissociative amnesia with a circumscribed phobic / conversion presentation.

- **Affect regulation.** Surface affect: warm, bright, sometimes vivacious; she is good at parties, good with Johnny's friends, good in public. Beneath: the panic channel activates roughly on schedule whenever its triggers are present. The pattern in FF #164–#179 is consistent: Johnny ignites, Frankie freezes / flees / dissociates / suppresses; later she returns, composed, with no acknowledgement of the episode and no curiosity about it. This non-curiosity is itself diagnostic — a person with an ordinary phobia *wonders* about it. Frankie does not. The conditioning includes a meta-block: she is conditioned not to investigate the phobia. Her affect regulation in this window is essentially *managed by the conditioning*; she does not regulate the panic, she waits it out while the conditioning re-seals.
- **Cognitive style.** Pragmatic, present-tense, externally oriented. She thinks about what is in front of her and acts on it. She does not narrate her inner life to herself or to Johnny. Her romantic decision-making — staying with Johnny despite the panic episodes, refusing him certain forms of intimacy without offering an explanation, sustaining the relationship in a state of permanent partial concealment — is *managed* rather than *examined*. This is the cognitive style of a person who has learned that some questions, when asked, produce intolerable distress; the system has trained itself to not ask.
- **Self-concept.** Performed and superficially confident. She presents as a young woman who knows who she is — name, parents, school, boyfriend, plans — and the presentation is convincing because she believes it. The somatic dissent (body-shame, refusal to be seen) registers to her as personal modesty or quirk rather than as evidence about her own history. The self-concept is *brittle but not yet fissured*; she is functioning, and she will continue to function until a sufficiently large external force breaches the conditioning. The structure has, in effect, been waiting for that force since she was a child.

**Hinge into Phase IV:** FF #190–#191 — the Horton confrontation, the discovery of the conditioning, the death of the father-figure, and the eruption of latent powers, all within a single compressed event.

---

## Phase IV — The Torch-II Period: FF #190/191 through #243 (~24 months published, narratively shorter)

The conditioning breaks. What should have produced a catastrophic decompensation produces, instead, a *too-clean* reorganization. This is the most diagnostically revealing phase, because the *speed and tidiness* of her recovery is itself the pathology.

- **Affect regulation.** Shifts abruptly from *dissociated/phobic* to *manically composed*. She is not seen mourning Horton. She is not seen mourning her own stolen childhood. She is not seen processing the revelation that her body is engineered. Within a publication-short interval she is cheerful, sexually confident with Johnny (the body-shame substrate evaporates the moment its source is named), eager to train, eager to fight. This is a textbook **manic defense** in Kleinian terms — a defense against depressive content (grief, mourning, integration of loss) by means of triumph, control, and contempt for the lost object. The lost object here is her entire pre-revelation self, and she handles its loss by *not having any feelings about it*. The affective channels that were split in Phase II–III now collapse into a single forward-facing register: bright, decisive, untroubled. The previous panic-channel content has been *transmuted*, not metabolized — she now generates flame rather than fearing it. The fear was never worked through; it was rewritten in the opposite direction.
- **Cognitive style.** Action-orientation now goes from coping mechanism to dominant operating mode. She makes the decision to adopt the powers, to adopt the *Torch* name, to enter the field as Johnny's partner, with no recorded period of deliberation. The cognitive style is now: *encounter event → categorize → act → do not revisit*. The Phase II–III meta-block on introspection now serves her actively — she has acquired a vast new body of material that would shatter any reflective person, and her conditioned non-reflection is exactly what allows her to keep moving. What was once a wound in her cognition has become her most adaptive trait. This is also, however, the cognitive style that disables every off-ramp that might have followed.
- **Self-concept.** The vacancy left by the collapse of the Phase II–III self is filled *immediately* with a borrowed identity: she becomes "the Human Torch," wearing her boyfriend's name. The choice is staggering when examined and unremarkable to her. She does not invent a name; she does not adopt her birth identity more fully; she does not retreat from the public role. She takes the role nearest to hand — defined by the man she is attached to — and inhabits it. This is the first overt instance of what becomes her lifelong pattern: when an identity is required, she takes the one offered by the most powerful person in her orbit. The self-concept of Phase IV is *Johnny's plus-one with matching powers*, and she experiences this as triumph rather than as the diminishment a more reflective person would recognize.

**Hinge into Phase V:** FF #244, the offering of a Herald. Crucially, no external compulsion. She volunteers. The volunteering is the key behavior of her entire arc.

---

## Phase V — The Herald Period: FF #244 through *Silver Surfer* #75 (cosmic duration unclear; ~decade of publication)

The reorganization completed in Phase IV is now *scaled* by the Power Cosmic and *consecrated* by attachment to Galactus. Every Phase IV pattern hardens.

- **Affect regulation.** Now organized at what can only be called a *post-human* level. The Power Cosmic, in every Herald case observed (Radd, Dargo, Pyreus, Gabriel), suppresses or recolors the endocrine substrate of ordinary affect. For Frankie this is *experienced as relief*, because the affective register being suppressed was the one in which her unprocessed grief and rage would otherwise have lived. She presents as serene, euphoric, devotional, untroubled. The flatness Surfer experiences as a loss she experiences as a gift. Affect regulation in Phase V is, paradoxically, *better than at any prior point* — but it is the stability of a system that has been freed from the obligation to feel rather than the stability of a system that has integrated its feelings. Under acute stress (the Surfer's moral challenges, the question of which world to feed Galactus) the only affective spike observed is *irritation* — and the irritation reliably appears precisely where her defenses are thinnest (when Radd questions the necessity of her loyalty).
- **Cognitive style.** Action-orientation now scaled to galactic decisions. She selects worlds for Galactus with the same uninvestigated decisiveness with which she once accepted the Torch name. The moral cognition is structured by **splitting and re-categorization**: targets are sorted into deserving (Skrulls, "monsters") and not-considered (everyone else, who is simply not present in her moral field). This is not a sophisticated moral philosophy; it is the same Phase II non-investigation habit applied to ethics — *categories that would produce distress are not examined*. Her cognitive style is now formally **morally disengaged** in Bandura's sense, with all four classical disengagement mechanisms observable: moral justification ("Galactus must feed"), euphemistic labeling ("preparation," "service"), dehumanization of victims ("monsters"), and displacement of responsibility (Galactus chooses, she only carries). Her intelligence is undimmed; it is *deployed* to maintain the structure rather than to question it.
- **Self-concept.** Now fully exteriorized and fully borrowed. She is **Nova, Herald of Galactus** — a name given by her patron, a role defined by her patron, a purpose supplied by her patron. The Phase IV vacancy filled by Johnny's name is now refilled by Galactus's designation, and the upgrade is felt as completion rather than as further erosion. Critically, she now possesses what she has never had before: *consistency between her stated self and her somatic self*. The body that was engineered for flame is finally inhabiting flame at the scale it was built for; the dissociation between the performed self and the somatic self that ran throughout Phase II–IV is, for the first time in her life, *closed*. This is why she is happy. The closure was achieved by surrendering authorship entirely to Galactus — but having never had authorship in any prior phase, surrender does not feel like loss.

The structure's brittleness shows only in two places across the entire Herald period: (1) she cannot tolerate the Surfer's moral seriousness as anything other than weakness — she cannot let it be a real critique, because if it were real she would have to revisit everything; (2) she has no observed period of solitary, unassigned existence. Whenever she is not on a mission, she is *en route* to one. Idle time is not depicted because idle time is the one condition her structure cannot survive.

**Terminus:** Morg's blade. Her death is sudden, externally caused, mid-flight, mid-mission — i.e., she dies in the only configuration her psychology could sustain, never having had to face the configuration it could not.

---

## Cross-Phase Synthesis: What Evolved, What Did Not

**Affect regulation** evolved from *split and conditioning-managed* (Phase II–III) → *manically reorganized* (Phase IV) → *post-humanly suppressed and experienced as relief* (Phase V). The trajectory is consistent: at every transition, the solution to unbearable affect is to *change the substrate that produces affect* rather than to process the content. She never grieves; she upgrades the operating system.

**Cognitive style** evolved very little in *kind* and enormously in *scale*. The Phase II habit of not-looking, originally imposed by Horton's conditioning, became the Phase III managed avoidance, then the Phase IV manic forward-motion, then the Phase V cosmic moral disengagement. It is the same habit at every scale, deployed against progressively larger content. Her intelligence is constant; what shifts is the magnitude of what her intelligence is being used to *not* examine.

**Self-concept** evolved through serial overwriting by progressively more powerful patrons: *Horton's daughter (false)* → *Johnny's girlfriend (true but partial)* → *the Human Torch (Johnny's name)* → *Nova, Herald of Galactus (Galactus's name)*. Each transition is experienced by her as liberation, and each transition further externalizes the locus of her identity. The endpoint — full identification with a cosmic devourer's purpose — is the logical completion of a developmental sequence in which she was never permitted, and never seized, the opportunity to author herself.

The single longitudinal finding that organizes the entire file: *Frankie Raye's psychology did not deteriorate over time; it executed*. The architecture laid down in Phase II ran to its terminus without ever being challenged by the only thing that could have interrupted it — sustained, supported, unhurried examination of what had been done to her. No such window ever opened. She moved too fast, the next patron arrived too soon, and the Power Cosmic eventually closed the door on the affective register in which such examination would have had to occur. What looks like character development across the published record is, on close inspection, the *same person at every age*, given progressively more powerful tools to maintain the same defensive posture. Her death does not interrupt a trajectory; it ratifies one.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL
## Subject: Frances "Frankie" Raye / Nova (Herald of Galactus)
## Prepared as: Longitudinal psychiatric formulation, behavior-derived

---

## I. FRAMING NOTE ON METHOD

The subject presents a rare opportunity in psychiatric formulation: an *iatrogenic* developmental trauma whose etiology is documented in the record (Phineas Horton's pediatric chemical-and-hypnotic conditioning, *Fantastic Four* #190–191), rather than inferred. This allows differential reasoning to proceed unusually cleanly. What follows treats DSM-5 / ICD-11 categories as *behavioral templates*, not as ontologies, and works strictly from observable conduct across the published longitudinal record (*FF* #164 through *Silver Surfer* #75, with periodic posthumous appearances). No diagnosis is asserted that is not behaviorally substantiated; comorbid features are flagged where the data is suggestive but not decisive; and the differential section is given disproportionate weight because the subject's surface presentation invites at least four plausible misdiagnoses that, on closer reading, do not survive scrutiny.

A standing methodological caution: the Power Cosmic conversion (post-*FF* #244) is a profound endocrinological/neurological event. It almost certainly suppresses or rewrites baseline human affective signaling. Any Axis-I/II picture drawn from Nova-period behavior must be read through that filter: we are looking at her *psychology operating on altered substrate*, not at uncomplicated human pathology. Where her pre-Nova baseline and her Nova behavior align, the trait is structural; where they diverge, the conversion is doing work.

---

## II. PRIMARY DIAGNOSTIC PICTURE — PHASE I (Pre-Revelation, c. childhood through *FF* #189)

### Principal: Dissociative Amnesia with Specific Phobic Surface (DSM-5 300.12 analog / ICD-11 6B61)

**Substantiating behavior.** From her first appearance (*FF* #164) through the Wolfman/Pollard arc, the subject exhibits a tightly circumscribed amnestic block surrounding a specific autobiographical domain — the pediatric Horton procedures — with the somatic memory of those procedures returning as a *specific phobia of fire* (ICD-11 6B03; DSM-5 300.29, natural environment subtype). The phobia is not freestanding: it is the surface eruption of the underlying amnesia. Critically, this is **iatrogenic dissociation** — produced by deliberate hypnotic conditioning rather than self-protective psychic splitting in response to discrete trauma — but the *clinical surface* is indistinguishable from spontaneously generated dissociative amnesia of trauma origin. The disorder resolves abruptly and apparently completely on confrontation with the conditioning agent (Horton himself), which is itself diagnostic: spontaneous dissociative amnesias rarely lift so cleanly, but iatrogenic hypnotic blocks regularly do when the conditioning frame is broken.

**Symptomatic features observed.**

- *Autonomic.* Tachycardia, freezing, blanching, hyperventilation on fire stimuli including Johnny's transformation (a stimulus she has consented to be repeatedly around — exposure does not extinguish, which is itself unusual and consistent with a *conditioned non-extinguishable* response rather than ordinary phobic learning).
- *Cognitive.* Inability to articulate the source of the fear; no narrative content to the panic; "I just *can't*" phrasing — characteristic of conditioned somatic response without accessible declarative memory.
- *Behavioral.* Avoidance not only of flame but of *contexts in which flame might appear* — including, notably, intimate physical contexts (refusal to be seen undressed, refusal of certain forms of touch). This generalization beyond the nominal phobic object indicates the phobia is a *placeholder* for a broader body-shame substrate, not a discrete fear of flame.
- *Functional.* Otherwise high-functioning, socially fluent, no global cognitive impairment, no other dissociative phenomena (no fugue, no depersonalization episodes reported, no identity fragmentation).

**Comorbid features, Phase I.** Subclinical body dysmorphic features (the conviction that her body is "wrong" without conscious content — see her sexual/intimate guarding); subclinical features of what might be called **somatic foreboding** — a chronic, low-grade conviction that something is amiss with her physical self, which she rationalizes as modesty. No mood disorder is observable in this period; her presentation is *bright surface over hollow content*, a configuration that will persist.

---

## III. PRIMARY DIAGNOSTIC PICTURE — PHASE II (Post-Revelation / Second Torch Period, *FF* #190 through #244)

### Principal: Trauma- and Stressor-Related Disorder, atypical course, with "flight into power" presentation

This is the phase that resists clean DSM-5 coding because the subject's response *to* the trauma resolution is itself the pathological picture. There is no clear PTSD (DSM-5 309.81) by standard criteria: no intrusion symptoms documented, no avoidance of trauma-related stimuli (she actively seeks them — she literally clothes herself in flame), no negative cognitions about self in the depressive register, no hypervigilance. By ICD-11's broader framework, however, she meets criteria for **Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (6B41)** with the three core C-PTSD features expressed in an *inverted, defended* form:

1. **Affect dysregulation** — present, but inverted: not lability or rage but suspiciously *flat positive affect*. She is too cheerful, too quickly, after a revelation that would devastate. The absence of grief is the symptom.
2. **Negative self-concept** — present, but compensated: she does not present negative self-cognitions; she presents a *constructed* positive self-concept built around the very alterations done to her. The negative self-concept is *operative* (she has no autonomous self to defend), but it is *masked* by adopted identity (the Second Torch persona, literally named after her boyfriend).
3. **Interpersonal disturbance** — present, classically: rapid serial attachment to dominant figures (Horton → Johnny → Galactus), no observable peer mutuality, inability to function without an organizing patron.

**The behavior that best operationalizes the diagnosis: identification with the aggressor as a coping strategy.** This is Anna Freud's mechanism, not a DSM category, but it is the most clinically useful description of what she does. The subject does not work through Horton's violation; she *completes* it. She becomes the successful version of his experiment and reframes the outcome as her choice. This is a recognizable, well-documented trauma response in survivors of long-duration covert abuse by caregivers — particularly when the abuse produced *real capacities or status* that the survivor can leverage. The capacity reframes the abuse.

**Comorbid features, Phase II.**

- **Manic defense.** Her bright, decisive, sexually confident, eager presentation in the immediate aftermath of the Horton revelation has the structure of a manic defense against grief and identity collapse — not bipolar mania (no pressured speech, no grandiose delusion, no decreased need for sleep, no impulsive financial or sexual disinhibition beyond baseline). It is a defensive elevation of mood that prevents collapse, sustained for as long as the supporting structure (Johnny, the Torch identity, the team) holds.
- **Subclinical depersonalization, intermittent.** Her ease in adopting a body whose true nature she has just learned was engineered without her consent suggests the body is not, for her, the locus of "self" in the ordinary way. This is not full DPDR (300.6) but reflects a long-standing somatic distance produced by the conditioning.
- **No substance use, no eating disorder, no overt mood episode.**

---

## IV. PRIMARY DIAGNOSTIC PICTURE — PHASE III (Nova / Herald Period, *FF* #244 through *Silver Surfer* #75)

This phase requires the most careful framing. The Power Cosmic conversion is a confounding variable of the first magnitude: it alters neurochemistry, suspends ordinary biological need, and demonstrably recolors affect in every Herald on record (Surfer's documented anhedonia and moral over-saturation; Firelord's emotional flattening; Terrax's amplified aggression on a pre-existing aggressive substrate; Air-Walker's mechanized loyalty). The general principle observed across Heralds is that **the Power Cosmic does not erase the underlying personality; it amplifies its dominant structural feature while suppressing the human affective register that would moderate it.** For the Surfer, that meant amplified moral seriousness without the human capacity to bear it lightly. For Frankie, it means amplified devotional loyalty and amplified moral disengagement, with the affective register that would have produced doubt, guilt, or grief substantially muted.

### Principal: Acquired Sociomoral Disengagement, scaffolded by Idealizing Attachment, on a substrate of disorganized attachment

This is not a DSM category. It must be assembled from several:

- **Persistent features of Complex PTSD (ICD-11 6B41)** — the underlying structure does not resolve; it is rendered ego-syntonic by the conversion.
- **Acquired Personality Change after Catastrophic Experience (ICD-11 6B66 analog)**, the catastrophic experience here being the *combined* Horton revelation and the Herald conversion. The criteria require a persistent change in personality lasting more than two years, with features including hostile or distrustful attitude toward the world (recoded here as *contemptuous indifference*), social withdrawal (recoded as *withdrawal from peer humanity into devotional fusion*), feelings of emptiness or hopelessness (present, masked by mission), chronic feeling of being "on edge" (absent — replaced by devotional serenity), and estrangement (present at cosmic scale). She meets at least three of the five with substitutions appropriate to her unusual trajectory.
- **Features of Shared / Induced Belief Pattern (folie à deux analog, ICD-10 F24, dropped in DSM-5 but clinically useful)** — her moral universe is now Galactus's, taken on whole; she defends it without independent derivation. With a population of two and a power differential of effectively infinite magnitude, the dyad is the smallest possible cult.

**The Skrull throneworld behavior (*Silver Surfer* #75 and the run preceding) is the diagnostic centerpiece of this phase.** Her enthusiasm at selecting populated worlds, her satisfaction at the Skrull genocide, her contempt for the Surfer's hesitation — none of these are *psychopathic* in presentation (see differential below). They are *ideologically organized*. She has a *reason*; she has a *frame*; she has *categories* (Skrulls = "monsters" = morally discountable). This is moral disengagement (Bandura's framework) operating at full strength, scaffolded by an attachment whose stability depends on her not questioning it. The cruelty is, in a deep sense, a *byproduct* of the loyalty rather than its goal.

**Affective presentation.** A serene, even euphoric, devotional steadiness. Not flat — there is positive affect. Not labile. Not anxious. Not angry. The only spike on record is *irritation at the Surfer* — which is structurally important: he threatens her resolution.

---

## V. COMORBIDITY ASSESSMENT (Across Phases)

- **Mood disorders (depressive spectrum).** *Absent in observable presentation across all phases.* This is itself notable; a person with her history would be expected to show major depressive episodes, particularly in Phase II. The absence is consistent with the manic-defense / flight-into-power dynamic; depression is what would happen if the defense collapsed, and the defense does not collapse before her death.
- **Bipolar spectrum.** *Absent.* Her elevated affect in Phase II is reactive and defensive, not episodic or autonomous.
- **Anxiety disorders.** *Phase-limited.* The Phase I specific phobia resolves. No generalized anxiety in subsequent phases; if anything, an abnormal *absence* of anxiety given her circumstances.
- **OCD spectrum.** *Absent.*
- **Eating disorders.** *Absent on record.* The body-shame features of Phase I do not translate into disordered eating; they translate into intimate avoidance.
- **Substance use.** *Absent.* The pediatric chemical exposure was non-consensual and is the etiology, not a comorbidity.
- **Psychotic spectrum.** *Absent.* No hallucinations, no formal thought disorder, no primary delusions. Her Nova-period beliefs about Skrulls and about Galactus's prerogative are *culturally shared* within the dyad she has joined and are *internally coherent*; they are ideological, not psychotic.
- **Neurocognitive.** *Confounded by Power Cosmic.* Pre-conversion: no impairment. Post-conversion: cognitive capacity expanded, not reduced; integration with substrate is uncomplicated.
- **Dissociative spectrum, post-Phase I.** *Subclinical somatic distance persists*; full dissociative disorder does not.

---

## VI. DIFFERENTIAL DIAGNOSIS — RIGOROUS EXCLUSIONS

The Nova-period behavior is inflammatory enough that several diagnoses get reached for and must be ruled out with care. Each of the following has been considered and rejected on the indicated evidence.

### 1. Antisocial Personality Disorder / Primary Psychopathy — RULED OUT

The cosmic-scale harm she enables is the strongest pull toward this diagnosis, and it must be the first excluded. ASPD (DSM-5 301.7) requires a *pervasive pattern* of disregard for the rights of others *since age 15*, with conduct disorder evidence before that age. Primary psychopathy (Hare PCL-R framework) requires shallow affect, glibness, callousness, lack of remorse, criminal versatility, parasitic lifestyle, and — critically — these features as *lifelong, structural* traits.

**Frankie fails the lifetime-course criterion decisively.** Her pre-revelation behavior across *FF* #164–#189 shows normal-range empathy, normal-range guilt, normal-range warmth toward Johnny, normal social reciprocity. Her harm-doing is *acquired*, *contextual* (specific to her Herald role), *ideologically framed*, and *attachment-driven* — none of which are features of primary psychopathy, in which harm-doing is *instrumental*, *opportunistic*, and *unmotivated by attachment* (psychopaths characteristically *cannot* bond at the depth Frankie bonds with Galactus). She also lacks the criminal versatility, the parasitic interpersonal pattern, and the impulsivity. Her cruelty as Nova is *organized*; psychopathic cruelty is *expressive*.

### 2. Narcissistic Personality Disorder — RULED OUT

A second tempting misdiagnosis, given the grandiosity of her cosmic role. NPD (DSM-5 301.81) requires *self-generated* grandiosity, a need for admiration as a primary motivation, exploitative interpersonal patterns *in service of self-aggrandizement*, and envy.

**Frankie's grandiosity is entirely borrowed.** She does not seek admiration; she seeks *to serve*. The aggrandizement she enjoys is reflected from Galactus, not generated. She does not envy peers; she is structurally indifferent to peers. Her exploitative behavior at cosmic scale is not in service of her self-image but in service of her patron's literal hunger. This is the photographic negative of NPD: NPD uses others to inflate the self; Frankie uses the self to feed the other.

### 3. Borderline Personality Disorder — RULED OUT

The serial attachment shifts (Horton → Johnny → Galactus) could superficially suggest BPD (DSM-5 301.83). The diagnosis fails on every other criterion: no chronic emptiness expressed as *suffering* (the emptiness is present but ego-syntonic, not dysphoric); no impulsive self-damaging behavior (her one massive impulsive decision — Herald acceptance — is calm and considered, not affectively driven); no recurrent suicidality or self-mutilation; no affective instability of the BPD type (her affect is too *stable*, in the wrong direction); no inappropriate intense anger; no transient stress-related paranoia or dissociation in adulthood; *and most decisively*, no relational push-pull. BPD attachments oscillate between idealization and devaluation of the *same* object. Frankie's attachments are *serially* idealizing, with the prior object cleanly released rather than oscillated against. The structural difference is large.

### 4. Dissociative Identity Disorder — RULED OUT

Her Phase I amnesia, taken alone, could superficially suggest DID (DSM-5 300.14). It is not: her amnesia is *circumscribed* to a specific autobiographical domain, *resolves* on confrontation, and is *not* accompanied by alternate identities, time loss in adult life, internal voices, or any of the other DID positive features. This is dissociative amnesia, not DID.

### 5. Bipolar I or II — RULED OUT

The elevated mood and decisive action of Phase II could be mistaken for hypomania. It is not: it is reactive, defensive, sustained without cycling, and lacks the autonomic and cognitive features of true mood elevation (no decreased need for sleep, no pressured speech, no flight of ideas, no grandiose delusions, no impulsive disinhibition beyond the single Herald decision, which is not impulsive in the bipolar sense — she has had weeks to consider it).

### 6. Schizophrenia-spectrum / Delusional Disorder — RULED OUT

Her Nova-period worldview is unusual but not psychotic. It is *shared* with her patron (which is the test that distinguishes ideological commitment from delusion: delusion is *idiosyncratic*); it is *internally coherent*; it is *responsive to evidence* within its frame (her contempt for the Surfer is *argued*, not asserted axiomatically). She has no hallucinations, no thought disorder, no negative symptoms.

### 7. Cult-induced / Coercive Persuasion Syndrome — PARTIALLY APPLICABLE BUT INSUFFICIENT

The folie à deux / shared belief framework captures real features of her Nova period (see §IV), but underspecifies the picture because Frankie *brought* the substrate for fusion to the dyad. She was not converted by Galactus from a robust autonomous self; she arrived with a vacancy that Galactus filled. Coercive-persuasion frameworks assume an intact prior self to be overwritten. Frankie's case is the reverse: a missing prior self being supplied. This is a meaningful clinical distinction and is why this diagnosis is partial.

### 8. Stockholm Syndrome (informal) — PARTIALLY APPLICABLE BUT INSUFFICIENT

Captures the affective bond with the harming patron but not the *developmental* etiology. Stockholm dynamics arise in adults captured intact; Frankie's bond template was laid down pre-verbally by Horton and was structurally complete before Galactus appeared. Galactus did not capture her; he received her.

### 9. Dependent Personality Disorder — PARTIALLY APPLICABLE

DPD (DSM-5 301.6) captures real features: the need for an organizing other, the discomfort with solitude-without-mission, the difficulty initiating independent action. It underspecifies the harm-doing and overspecifies the *anxious* quality typical of DPD, which Frankie lacks. Best read as a *personality-organization feature* within a broader picture, not a standalone diagnosis.

---

## VII. INTEGRATED FORMULATION

The most accurate single-line psychiatric formulation, supported by the longitudinal behavior, is:

> **An iatrogenic dissociative amnesia with phobic surface (Phase I), resolving into a Complex PTSD presentation with atypical identification-with-aggressor course and manic-defense features (Phase II), consolidating under cosmic biological alteration into an acquired sociomoral disengagement scaffolded by idealizing fusion-attachment to a singular patron (Phase III), on a foundational substrate of disorganized attachment and dependent personality organization produced by pediatric covert abuse by the primary caregiver.**

The course over time is *progressive* in the sense that each phase consolidates rather than resolves the underlying structure: the phobia lifts, but the disorganized attachment that produced its substrate does not; the manic defense holds, but the empty self it defends is not rebuilt; the cosmic conversion silences the affective register that would have eventually broken the defense down, allowing the defended structure to persist unchallenged until her death.

The prognosis, had she lived, would have been guarded. The Surfer's persistent presence in her orbit constituted the only ongoing therapeutic-like pressure on her structure — he embodied the alternative resolution she had foreclosed, and her irritation at him was the closest she came to the productive disturbance that precedes integration. Morg's blade in *Silver Surfer* #75 foreclosed that trajectory.

---

## VIII. KEY POINTS FOR FILE

- The cosmic-scale harm is *not* evidence of primary psychopathy. The structural diagnosis is closer to *over-loyal cult member with attachment-trauma substrate* than to *predator*.
- Her cheerfulness is real, her courage is real, and her cruelty is real; all three are produced by the same underlying mechanism (defense of a fusion-attachment that her self-coherence depends on).
- The one stimulus consistently observed to disturb her constructed equilibrium is *moral seriousness from a peer she cannot dismiss*. This is the file's recommended pressure point in any hypothetical recovery scenario.
- The phrase "she became the thing that was done to her" is not metaphor in this file. It is the operative clinical mechanism.


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS: FRANCES "FRANKIE" RAYE / NOVA

## Classification: Volume III — Longitudinal Tell-Catalog, All Conditions

---

## Preface to the Atlas

What follows is a granular registry of Subject's observable behavior across the documented arc — civilian (FF #164 onward), trainee/Second Torch (FF #190 onward), Herald (FF #244 through SS #75) — sorted by condition and cross-indexed against era so the same act can be read against itself over time. The Atlas privileges micro-tells: the small involuntary signatures the dossier-keeper would weight more heavily than declared statements, because Subject is a person whose conscious statements are unusually congruent with her conscious self-image and unusually incongruent with the structural facts of her life. The body, the eyes, the hands, the breath, and the timing of her decisions carry the real signal.

---

## 1. BASELINE / CALM

**Civilian era (pre-revelation).** At rest, Subject reads as well-socialized and uncomplicated. Posture upright but slightly forward-canted; she leans into whomever is speaking, an attentive listener-orientation that flatters and is rewarded with disclosure. Voice in the middle register, fluent, very few filler words; she does not stammer or grope for sentences in ordinary talk. Eye contact is steady and warm — almost a beat too long, which civilians experience as charisma. She smiles with the eyes as well as the mouth, but a sustained-frame analysis would show the smile drops between conversational beats faster than baseline, snapping back when re-addressed: the social face is a deliberate performance, not a resting state. At rest-rest — i.e., when alone, unobserved, sitting on Johnny's couch, waiting — her face is *flat*, almost still. Not sad; vacant. The vacancy is the tell.

Hands: she does small, repetitive things with them — straightens a sleeve, recurls a lock of hair, tucks the same lock again — a low-grade self-soothing baseline that does not register as anxiety because it is so continuous. She wears long sleeves and high collars in civilian dress more often than the weather requires; this remains true through the Torch period, where it has no power-related rationale and is therefore residue of the pre-revelation body-shame substrate.

**Second Torch era.** Calm baseline is louder, brighter, more performed. The body opens up — she laughs more readily, gestures larger, stands with hands on hips in the Torch flightsuit-equivalent posture that is openly modeled on Johnny's. The vacancy at rest-rest is still there but harder to catch because she now manufactures activity to fill it: she trains, she goes flying, she initiates social plans. *Subject does not sit still in this period.* That is itself the tell. Compare against the pre-revelation Subject, who would sit on the couch for an hour with the same look on her face.

**Herald era.** Baseline affect is a slow, low-amplitude serenity. Eyes long-focused at middle distance; speech cadence slowed by perhaps a third; gestures rare, economical, gravity-free in the literal sense. The face at rest has no vacancy now because Subject is no longer running a social-mask routine — she is genuinely composed, the way the Surfer is composed, only without his sorrow. The micro-tic of fingers-on-fabric is gone; there is no fabric, and her hands rest in postures that recall iconography of saints (open, lowered, palms slightly turned). This is the most relaxed Subject has ever appeared on the record.

---

## 2. STRESS (subliminal, non-threatening — workload, social complexity, ambiguity)

**Civilian.** Three signatures. (1) She redirects conversations away from her past. A question about her mother, her stepfather, her childhood home, what she studied — any of these reliably produces a topic-pivot within two exchanges, usually executed by asking the questioner about themselves. The pivot is so fluid that interlocutors register it as graciousness. (2) She develops a small swallow-tic when stress accumulates — visible throat motion between sentences, sometimes followed by a sip of whatever drink is at hand even if she does not need it. (3) Color rises high on the cheekbones, not the jaw — a pyrophobic flushing pattern interesting in retrospect: the body warms in distress, which is also what the body fears.

**Second Torch.** Stress is masked by acceleration. She talks faster, decides faster, volunteers for more. Where the civilian Subject deflected, the Torch-era Subject *outruns*. Watch for her offering to take a task off someone else's plate — this is altruism on the surface and stress-discharge underneath. She also fire-flicks: small, involuntary plasma sparks at the fingertips when she is concentrating on something difficult, a tell she never fully controls.

**Herald.** Subliminal stress is rare and presents as a single repeated mannerism — a slow tilt of the head, perhaps fifteen degrees, held for a beat longer than a conversational tilt would warrant, as if she is listening to something on a frequency the speaker cannot hear. Functionally this is her checking Galactus's distant signal, but it surfaces under any conversational pressure, not only when he calls. It is her displacement gesture.

---

## 3. ACUTE STRESS / PHOBIC FLOODING (civilian era only)

The signature event of the early file. Trigger: open flame in proximity, especially Johnny's transformation, but also matches, gas stoves, fireplace, a candle held too close. Sequence is consistent across episodes:

1. **Freeze, ~1 second.** Eyes lock on the flame; pupils blow wide; the breath stops mid-cycle.
2. **Withdraw, ~1–2 seconds.** Trunk pulls backward before the legs move, an involuntary recoil; arms come up in a half-shield posture not consciously chosen.
3. **Flight initiation, ~3 seconds.** She turns and *moves*, fast, often without a verbal explanation; if cornered, she presses against the farthest available surface.
4. **Apologia, post-event.** Once the flame is gone she returns to baseline within thirty seconds and offers a self-deprecating account ("I don't know what's wrong with me"). She does not cry. She does not seek comfort. She *closes the topic*, which is the same redirect-pattern observed under low stress, applied to her own incident.

Notable: she is never observed seeking professional help for the phobia and does not bring it up unprompted between episodes. The phobia exists for her only when triggered; she has no narrative of it. This is consistent with the conditioning — the affect was implanted without an autobiographical hook to hang it on.

---

## 4. THREAT (someone or something threatening her physically)

**Civilian.** No combat training, no fighting reflex. Under threat she calls for Johnny, freezes, or runs. She is not paralyzed in panic; she is a normal civilian under attack.

**Second Torch.** Subject's combat behavior is *imitative*. Her tactics, her flame-shapes, her aerial maneuvers all replicate Johnny's. She fires plasma-bursts at the same angles; she throws fireballs with the same windup; she even uses his catchphrase-energy. Her combat decisions during this period have a one-beat lag relative to Johnny's — she watches him move and then mirrors. Independent tactical decisions in this era are rare and tend toward the conservative (cover, suppress, support). She does not freelance.

**Herald.** Threat-response is a step-change. She does not flinch; she does not posture; she ends the engagement with the minimum-energy solution available to a being of her capacity, which means she tends to *overwhelm rather than spar*. Where the Surfer often de-escalates and bargains, Subject closes distance and applies overwhelming cosmic flame. She will not negotiate with a threat to herself; she has no patience for it. The contrast with her civilian flight response is exact — same person, same somatic urgency, opposite vector. The thing that used to make her run now makes her *finish*.

A revealing micro-tell during Herald-era combat: she smiles in the last second before the kill-stroke. Not a sneer; a small, almost private smile, the kind one wears when a long-rehearsed task finally goes right. Galactus's other heralds do not do this. The Surfer never did. This is hers.

---

## 5. INTIMACY (physical and emotional)

**Civilian era with Johnny.** Affectionate in public — hand on his arm, head on his shoulder, kisses of unremarkable duration. In private the pattern shifts. She manages lighting; she manages clothing; she manages proximity to his body when he runs warm or absent-mindedly low-flames. The unspoken contract is that he keeps the temperature down and she keeps the relationship pleasant. She is not observed initiating sexual contact in canon, and her demurrals when he initiates are framed as old-fashioned reserve. This is one of the cleanest examples of how her surface presentation re-coded a trauma symptom as a personality trait that read as charming. The body-guarding was *the wound speaking through the costume of propriety*.

Emotional intimacy is uneven. She listens superbly. She discloses thinly. Across the entire civilian period there is no scene of her telling Johnny — or anyone — something difficult about her interior life unprompted. She volunteers information about her day, her plans, her opinions of others; she does not volunteer information about her self.

**Second Torch era.** Physical reserve dissolves *abruptly* after the Horton confrontation, which is itself a tell — a person who had been guarding her body for sound psychological reasons does not, in healthy resolution, drop the guard within days. The dropping is a manic-defensive overcorrection. She is openly affectionate, takes Johnny's hand in public, talks about the future. The relational tone in this period is almost *prefab*: she is performing a recognizable Couple Script with skill.

Emotional intimacy in this era is paradoxically *worse*, because she now has a story to tell about her interior life (the trauma, the revelation, the rebirth as Torch) and she tells it the same way each time, with the same beats and the same conclusions. The polish indicates it is a closed narrative, not a process. Anyone listening for the seams would notice that she never disagrees with her own account, never revises, never says "I'm still figuring it out."

**Herald era.** Intimacy with humans ends. Her last extended interaction with Johnny before departure is brisk, kind, and final; she does not linger, does not cry, does not promise to return. Her intimacy now is vertical — with Galactus — and it is devotional rather than relational. Subject does not converse with Galactus as an equal; she attends, she serves, she anticipates. Her body language in his presence is the body language of an acolyte: head slightly bowed even when speaking, distance kept, never crowding the throne-space. When Galactus addresses her, her response latency is short — she has been listening.

With the Surfer, the only Herald-peer relationship on record, intimacy is impossible. She treats him with the impatience reserved for those who knew you when you were less.

---

## 6. GRIEF

This is the section with the most negative space, and the negative space is the data.

**On Horton's death.** Subject's reaction in the moment of Horton's killing is shock, then accelerated processing toward *rebirth narrative* within the same arc. There is no funeral scene, no mourning sequence, no return to a grave, no anniversary marker, no recorded conversation in which she names what she lost. The man who raised her and the man who violated her are the same man and she does not have separate accounts for them; she has *no account for either of them after the moment of death*. This is, diagnostically, the absence of grief — not its suppression. Suppressed grief leaks at predictable junctures (anniversaries, holidays, sleep). Subject's grief does not leak because the conditioning created a self that lacked the autobiographical scaffolding on which grief mounts.

**On leaving Johnny / leaving Earth.** No observed grief. She departs Earth with a Herald's transformed serenity already coming on; her last words are not yearning. Reread by anyone who loved her, those last words would scan as cold; in the moment, they scan as transcendent.

**On the destruction of inhabited worlds.** No grief, by structure of her chosen role. The interesting tell is that she does not even perform the conventional minimum of "regret-but-necessity" that the Surfer used to perform. She skips that beat. She moves directly to selection-and-pride.

**On her own approaching death (SS #75 sequence).** No fear-grief observed; she is killed too quickly for an arc, but her behavior in the lead-up shows no premonitory withdrawal, no settling of affairs, no reaching out to Earth. She dies inside the role.

A reasonable inference: Subject does not grieve because she does not, in the technical sense, possess the continuous self that grieving requires. To grieve a loss you must locate the loss inside a continuous you that existed before and persists after. Subject's selves are *replaced*, not *continuous* — civilian Frankie is replaced by Torch Frankie is replaced by Nova. Each replacement is an escape from the previous, and the previous is not mourned because it is not claimed.

---

## 7. VICTORY

**Civilian.** Subject does not have a victory mode in the conventional sense; her small wins (social, romantic) are met with bright affect and quick generosity — she shares the moment, deflects credit, asks the other person about themselves. This is socially attractive and characterologically consistent: she does not enjoy being the focus.

**Second Torch.** Victory after a fight registers as elation and physical exuberance — flight loops, fireworks, laughter. She accepts credit *with* Johnny, not alone; she does not seek the solo spotlight. There is a recurrent post-combat micro-behavior: she touches the back of her own neck briefly, almost a self-check, as if confirming her body is intact. This may be conditioning-residue — the body-monitoring habit of someone whose body was once not-her-own.

**Herald.** Victory in the Herald sense — successful provision of a world to Galactus — registers as deep, quiet satisfaction. The smile observed in combat returns, longer-held. She does not celebrate visibly because there is no peer to celebrate with; she returns to Galactus's presence and is, briefly, *closer*. Closeness to the patron is the only reward she still recognizes.

---

## 8. DEFEAT / SETBACK

**Civilian.** A social rebuff, a misread, a small humiliation: she absorbs it with grace and re-routes. She does not retaliate, does not sulk, does not litigate. She also does not raise the matter later. Defeats are filed and closed.

**Second Torch.** Tactical defeats in combat — being knocked down, missing a target, being outmaneuvered — produce a tight-jaw moment and an immediate re-engagement, often with increased intensity. She does not retreat to regroup; she retries the move that failed. This is a recognizable pattern in people who cannot tolerate a self-image of incompetence: continuation is preferable to reassessment. The fire-flick at the fingertips is more pronounced after such moments.

**Herald.** Defeat is functionally absent until the final encounter with Morg, which is over too quickly to be a defeat-arc. But: across the Herald years, on the rare occasions she is contradicted or her selections are challenged (most notably by the Surfer), her response is not the bright re-route of civilian Frankie nor the re-engagement of Torch Frankie. It is *derision* — an unusual and revealing escalation. The dossier-keeper should weight derision-responses heavily. They mark the locations where Subject's worldview is structurally unable to absorb the input.

---

## 9. DECISION HABITS (cross-era)

A consistent decision-architecture is detectable across all three eras and is one of the file's clearest through-lines.

- **Latency: short.** Subject decides quickly. The volunteer-for-Herald moment, the adopt-the-Torch-identity moment, the take-Horton's-revelation-and-move-forward moment, the cross-the-room-toward-Johnny moments — all are executed with low deliberation latency. She is not impulsive in the chaotic sense; she is *pre-decided*. Her decisions feel fast because the question "what kind of person am I" was answered for her by Horton, and most subsequent decisions are corollaries.
- **Direction: toward the larger gravity well.** When two paths are available, she selects the one that binds her more tightly to the more powerful figure in the situation. This is invariant.
- **Reversibility preference: irreversible.** She prefers decisions she cannot undo (rebrand, leave Earth, accept Herald conversion). Reversible decisions leave open the question of who she is; irreversible decisions answer it.
- **Consultation: minimal.** She rarely asks. She informs. When she does ask (Reed, occasionally), the question is logistical, not strategic.
- **Post-decision rumination: absent.** She does not revisit. Once chosen, a path is the path.
- **Risk tolerance: extreme for self, asymmetric for others.** She accepts massive personal risk without negotiation; she also accepts massive risk *to strangers* without negotiation, particularly in the Herald period.

---

## 10. SOMATIC AND HABITUAL MICRO-PATTERNS (longitudinal registry)

- **Hand-to-hair tuck (civilian, intermittent through Torch era).** A specific gesture: right hand to the right side of the hair, tucking behind the ear, releasing. Frequency rises with social attention; appears in candid moments unprompted. Vestigial by Herald era (no hair in the human sense once cosmic).
- **Sleeve and collar preference (civilian through Torch era).** Long sleeves, high necks. Survives the loss of the body-shame rationale. A residue.
- **Throat-swallow under stress (civilian).** Visible enough to read on film if film existed; reliable subliminal-stress indicator.
- **Cheek flush, not jaw flush, under stress (civilian).** Specific pattern; useful for distinguishing genuine distress from social embarrassment, which flushes broader.
- **Fingertip plasma-flicker under concentration (Torch era).** Involuntary; she does not register it; observers do.
- **One-beat tactical lag behind Johnny (Torch era combat).** Reliable in pair-action; absent in solo action, where she defaults to conservative play.
- **Self-neck-touch post-combat (Torch era).** Body-check residue.
- **Smile pre-kill-stroke (Herald era).** The most consequential single tell in the entire file. Private, brief, real.
- **Head-tilt-and-hold (Herald era).** Displacement gesture; correlates with conversational pressure and with distant patron-signal monitoring; the two are not always distinguishable.
- **Acolyte body language in Galactus's presence (Herald era).** Slight bow at the neck; preserved distance; short response latency.
- **Topic-pivot to the interlocutor (all eras, attenuating).** Most fluent civilian-era, present but less needed Torch-era, rare Herald-era. The pivot was a defense against being asked about a self she did not have; once the role supplied a self, the defense relaxed.
- **Absence of laughter at her own expense (all eras).** Subject jokes; Subject does not let others joke about her. Quiet but consistent.
- **No documented private rituals.** No diary, no prayer, no recurring solitary walk, no anniversary observance, no kept photograph in any era. This is itself a category-tell: the file's empty drawer.

---

## 11. CROSS-CONDITION SYNTHESIS

The Atlas, read whole, describes a person whose body and decision-architecture are extraordinarily consistent across radically different conditions — *because* the underlying self is a vacancy organized around whichever patron currently fills it. Civilian Frankie, Torch Frankie, and Nova are not three developmental stages of one person; they are three coherent surfaces over the same shape. The tells migrate (hair-tuck → head-tilt; fingertip flicker → pre-kill smile) but the structure does not change: orient to the larger figure, decide fast, do not look back, do not grieve, do not sit alone without a task. The Atlas is, in the end, the registry of a person who learned in childhood that she would be safer if she did not have an interior to defend, and who, having learned it, never had to relearn it under any condition life put to her. Calm, stress, threat, intimacy, grief, victory, defeat — across all six, the same answer: *attach upward and proceed.*


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — FRANCES "FRANKIE" RAYE
## Section 7: Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

A surveillance file on this subject is unusual in that it spans three radically different *operating environments* — late-1970s civilian Manhattan, early-1980s Baxter Building–adjacent costumed life, and post-1982 cosmic itinerancy at Herald scale. The architecture of her days is different in each, but the underlying *temperament* governing how she fills time is continuous, and that continuity is itself the most revealing data. She is, across all three eras, a person who organizes her hours around an external schedule supplied by someone else — a school, a boyfriend's hero life, a cosmic master's hunger cycle — and who appears genuinely uncomfortable in any block of unstructured time. A week of watching her would record many things; the absence of *solitary self-directed leisure* would be the most striking.

---

### 7.1 The Civilian Era (Empire State / Manhattan, FF #164–#191)

**Sleep architecture.** Subject keeps a conventional college-student schedule on the surface — bed between 23:30 and 01:00, up by 08:00 or 08:30 on weekdays — but observation across multiple weeks would log a consistent pattern of *interrupted* sleep in the 03:00–04:30 window: lights coming back on, kitchenette activity, the radio turned low. She does not appear to remember these wakings well the next morning. The pyrophobic conditioning leaks out at night; she is a poor sleeper and underreports it. She sleeps in long sleeves and high collars in every season, including July. She does not sleep nude. She sleeps on her back, blankets pulled to the collarbone, and her bedside lamp — never the overhead — stays on at low wattage. No candles in the apartment. No gas range used; she has a hot plate and an electric kettle, both of which she watches the entire time they are on.

**Morning ritual.** Roughly forty minutes, the same sequence every day: bathroom, then coffee (instant, made with the electric kettle, never percolated), then she dresses with the closet door closed and the bedroom blinds down. She will not undress in any room with a window uncovered. She showers with the bathroom door locked even when alone in the apartment. Hair is brushed and styled at a small vanity using a battery mirror; the makeup palette is narrow and consistent — she does not experiment. She eats breakfast standing, usually toast and fruit, almost never sitting down at the table; sitting and eating alone seems to require more of her than she has in the morning.

**Workday / school day.** Classes at Empire State University, where she is enrolled alongside Johnny in this period. Attendance is reliable; grades implied to be solid but unremarkable. She walks the same route to and from campus, varying it only when construction forces her. She prefers the right side of the sidewalk, near buildings rather than near the curb (street-level fire risks — exhaust, hot dogs vendors, hot-asphalt smell — push her toward facades). She does not take the subway when she can avoid it; she has on at least three occasions walked twenty blocks rather than descend into a station where she once smelled an electrical burn. She eats lunch on campus, in the cafeteria, almost always with Johnny or with one of two female acquaintances whose names appear once each in dialogue and never recur — she does not maintain durable peer friendships.

**Evening with Johnny.** This is the structurally important block of her day. She organizes the late afternoon around when Johnny will be free; if he is on FF business she waits. She does not develop a parallel evening life of her own. Surveillance would log her at her own apartment reading, doing coursework, calling her mother on the kitchen phone (short calls, ten minutes, weekly, affectionate but not intimate — she does not discuss anything substantive about her life with her mother), and watching television at low volume. She watches comedies and game shows; she actively avoids news footage of fires (she will rise and change the channel, then sit back down without comment). Books on her shelves are paperback novels, romance and light mystery, plus textbooks; nothing about psychology, nothing about her own history, nothing about Horton's field.

When she does see Johnny it is at restaurants, his quarters at the Baxter Building, movies, dance clubs — Johnny chooses the venues; she goes along, animated and present. Physical intimacy is conducted entirely on her terms and her terms are restrictive: lights off, clothes mostly on, no fire, no transformation in her presence, no Torch tricks "to impress her." Johnny accommodates because he loves her; he reads her restrictions as modesty. Observation would suggest something more layered — a body she does not feel ownership of and cannot bear to expose to the gaze of someone who runs hot.

**Weekly rituals.** Sunday: long phone call with her mother (Carla Raye, married to Horton after Frankie's biological father's exit). Tuesday and Thursday evenings: she goes to the campus library and stays past closing, ostensibly for coursework, in practice because the library is the one large public space in her life where she sits alone and is at peace; the silence of a library is the closest she gets to solitary self-presence. Saturday: a daytime activity with Johnny — museum, park, drive out of the city. Sunday afternoons: alone, sometimes a movie matinée, sometimes nothing visible.

**Recurring micro-behaviors a watcher would log.**
- Touches the inside of her left wrist to her right palm when she passes a flame on the street — a self-soothing gesture she is unaware of.
- Holds her breath for two to three seconds when a stove is lit in her presence.
- Will not strike a match. Has never been observed lighting a candle, a cigarette, or a pilot light.
- Carries a small flashlight in her bag at all times; the bulb is replaced on a schedule.
- Wears a wristwatch on the right wrist — she is right-handed, which is unusual placement; the watch is positioned to cover a faint mark on the underside of the wrist that she has never explained and that, in retrospect, is plausibly an old chemical-exposure scar from Horton's procedures.
- Apologizes reflexively for small things — bumping into furniture, asking the waiter to repeat himself, taking longer than expected at a turnstile.
- Laughs slightly *before* a joke lands rather than after, a social-anticipation tic.

---

### 7.2 The Transitional Period — "Second Human Torch" (FF #203 through #244)

The discovery in #190–191 detonates the civilian routine. What is striking on surveillance is how *quickly* a new routine assembles in its place, and how few of the old tells disappear.

**Sleep.** Improves dramatically. She sleeps through the night for the first time in observable record. She continues to leave a low light on but appears to do so out of habit rather than need; if the bulb burns out she does not replace it urgently. She sleeps less — six hours suffices — and rises earlier, 06:00 or 06:30, with energy.

**Body and dress.** The collar-and-sleeves armor falls away within weeks. She begins wearing short sleeves, V-necks, and — once she is suited up — a flame-form skin. She is photographed in this period in costume far more than in civilian clothes; she has, in effect, replaced one full-coverage wardrobe (the phobic one) with another (the cosmetic-flame one), and is more comfortable in the latter. The shower-door is no longer locked. She and Johnny are intimate without the previous restrictions. The body she could not stand to be seen in has been *reclassified* as an instrument she can now display.

**Training.** Daily, on the Baxter Building's upper levels and over the Atlantic. Reed's logs would show flight drills, plasma-control exercises, and aerial maneuver coordination with Johnny. She is a fast study to the point of suspicion — she does not learn the powers so much as *remember* them, which corroborates that Horton's conditioning included motoric programming. She enjoys training. She is observed laughing in the air. This is a person discovering that her body, finally, does what she wants.

**Daily structure.** Mornings: training. Midday: coursework — she is finishing her degree in this period, attending in civilian clothes, but the academic discipline has loosened; her attention is elsewhere. Afternoons: more training, or FF mission support. Evenings: with Johnny, increasingly in public as a couple, increasingly photographed. She begins to appear in society columns. She does not seek the attention but she does not hide from it either.

**What does not change.** She still does not develop independent friendships. The phone calls home are *shorter* now, not longer — she has less to say to her mother because her life is now organized around a world her mother cannot enter. She still does not read about psychology, does not seek therapy (which the FF have access to via Reed's contacts and which Sue has discreetly used), does not visit Horton's grave, does not contact any of his colleagues to ask further questions about what was done to her. The investigation she might have undertaken into her own past she does not undertake. *Forward, not back* is the operating directive, and it is total.

**Rituals retained.** She still touches wrist to palm when passing flame she did not produce. She still does not strike matches — she lights things now by *being* the flame, not by transferring it. She still apologizes reflexively. She still sleeps on her back. The watch on the right wrist is gone — the costume covers it — but in civilian clothes the watch returns to the right wrist over the mark.

---

### 7.3 The Herald Era — Nova (post-FF #244 through SS #75)

This is where the file becomes both larger in scope and stranger in texture. "Daily life" is an inadequate frame; her existence is now organized around the **feeding cycle of Galactus**, which operates on a rhythm of weeks to months, punctuated by long stretches of stellar transit. But within that frame, recognizable routines persist, and they are revealing.

**The hunger-cycle as schedule.** Galactus's need to consume sets the basic tempo. Between feedings he ranges; she ranges ahead. A "week" in her existence might mean a week of FTL flight through a stellar arm, surveying systems, cataloging signatures, returning to him with options. She is *always on assignment* — there is no recorded period of Herald-Frankie at rest, idle, alone, doing nothing.
