**Tier 3 — Threat to the bond with the patron.** Galactus injured, depowered, disrespected, replaced by a competing herald. *Response:* zealotry. She accelerates the moral disengagement spiral — preferentially selecting worlds that can be easily reframed as monstrous (the Skrull Throneworld selection is the diagnostic case). The harm she does ratchets upward as the bond feels less secure, because each act of service is *evidence to herself* that the bond is real. This is the most dangerous operational tier: she is most lethal not when secure but when the bond is *contested*.

**Tier 4 — Forced confrontation with pre-Nova material.** Direct reminders of Horton; archived footage of her childhood; an unsought encounter with Johnny that invokes her as Frankie rather than as Nova; any framing of her body as Horton's artifact rather than her own elected instrument. *Response:* unknown in extended form, because the canon never sustains this pressure on her — but the brief beats that exist (the Horton confrontation itself in FF #190–191) show the diagnostic pattern: a brief affective spike (panic, then grief-without-tears), followed by an unnaturally rapid resolution-by-action (claim the powers, claim the name, move on). Under sustained Tier 4 pressure — pressure she cannot escape by mission — the substrate that the conditioning suppressed would have to be metabolized, and there is no evidence she possesses the apparatus to metabolize it.

**Tier 5 — Patron withdrawn or revealed as instrumentalizing in a way she cannot reframe.** Galactus dying, Galactus discarding her, Galactus exposed as having always intended her as disposable. *Response:* this is the structural break point. The entire scaffold — body authored by patron, role assigned by patron, ethics licensed by patron — collapses simultaneously, with no fallback identity beneath it.

**Tier 6 — Compelled stillness.** Solitude without mission, captivity without an external enemy to focus on, sensory deprivation, immobilization that prevents flight. This is the *worst* environment for her, worse than physical assault. Her psychology has no operating mode for unstructured time; the conditioning never installed one, and Horton, Johnny, and Galactus each provided continuous external structure. Compelled stillness produces the conditions under which the suppressed material has nowhere to go but back into consciousness.

## 3. The Decompensation Pattern — How the System Actually Fails

When the doubling-down curve finally fails to discharge the pressure, the failure does not look like a typical breakdown. It looks like the staged collapse of a structure that has no load-bearing self underneath. Predicted stages, in order:

**Stage A — Hyper-mission.** Before any visible cracking, an observable acceleration: she takes on more, flies further, finds worlds faster, displays more cosmic flame than the task requires. This is the system trying to outrun the pressure by maximizing its only working output. To an outside observer this looks like peak competence; it is in fact the first sign of failure.

**Stage B — Categorical brittleness.** Her moral re-coding of targets — "monsters," "in the way" — becomes coarser and more obvious. The categories stop tracking even the loose criteria she previously applied. Peers who try to challenge her receive responses that are scripted rather than engaged: the same phrases, the same dismissals. The personality begins running on cached output.

**Stage C — Affective leak.** The serene devotional steadiness develops anomalies. Brief flashes of an affect that does not belong to Nova: a flicker of the old phobia in proximity to certain fires, an inappropriate moment of warmth toward a target, a sudden refusal to be touched that has no Nova-period referent. These are the suppressed somatic memories of Frankie-pre-revelation surfacing through the cosmic-flattened endocrinology. She will not name them. She will not be able to name them. They will look, to her, like equipment malfunctions rather than feelings.

**Stage D — Bond panic.** Increased proximity-seeking toward the patron. Where she previously orbited Galactus with confident autonomy, she now hovers, checks in, seeks acknowledgment. The serenity gives way to a quieter, more anxious devotion. If the patron is unavailable, she will substitute mission intensity — *being maximally useful* as a proxy for being told she still belongs.

**Stage E — Identity vacuum exposure.** This is the genuine crisis. Some event — an enforced pause, a direct existential challenge from a figure she cannot dismiss, a moment of compelled stillness — forces her to attempt to articulate who she is independent of patron and mission. She cannot. The vacancy that the entire constructed self has been performing over becomes briefly perceptible to her. Predicted behavioral signature: a flat, unscripted moment of silence; a question she does not finish; a refusal to remain in the conversation; precipitous departure into the most extreme available mission. If departure is blocked, see Stage F.

**Stage F — Collapse-by-recursion.** With no exit into mission and no exit into patron, the structure has nothing left to perform. The likely presentation is *not* florid breakdown but a sudden affective and behavioral *blanking*: stillness, blunted speech, motoric slowing, an almost catatonic withdrawal. The Power Cosmic substrate will keep the body operational, but the personality system will be effectively absent. Recovery from Stage F is not predictable, because the personality has no prior stable state to return to — there is no Frankie-before-Horton to recover, and Frankie-after-Horton was always already a performance.

**Stage G — Re-bonding or hollowing.** If a new patron-figure presents during or shortly after Stage F, the system will likely re-form around that figure with startling speed — the substrate is *primed* to be re-authored, has been since age six or so. This is the most operationally significant prediction in this file: under collapse, Frankie does not become independent. She becomes *available for capture* by whatever powerful figure addresses her in patron-coded language during the window. If no such figure presents, the alternative is gradual hollowing — continued operation as Nova in form without the devotional content, a Herald-shaped automaton.

## 4. The Conditions That Produce Collapse — Operator's Checklist

Tabulated for the file, in rough order of decompensating power:

1. **Loss of Galactus** without immediate replacement bond. Highest-probability trigger. Her entire post-Earth architecture is hung from this hook.
2. **Demonstrated betrayal by Galactus** — evidence she was never chosen, only used, in terms she cannot reframe. More destructive than simple loss because it invalidates the dignity-narrative she built around the choice.
3. **Compelled extended encounter with Johnny Storm in a context where she must respond to him as Frankie.** Johnny is the only living figure with social standing to address the pre-Nova self; he is also a fire-figure, which means the somatic conditioning will fire in his presence in ways the Power Cosmic only partially suppresses.
4. **Re-encounter with Horton's work or legacy** — archived materials, surviving collaborators, a recovered procedural record, the original Hammond android in a context that invokes their shared substrate. This pressure attacks the foundation directly.
5. **Captivity, immobilization, or sensory isolation.** Removes mission as a discharge route; forces the system to run idle.
6. **A morally serious peer she cannot dismiss in a context she cannot leave.** Surfer-class pressure, sustained, in close quarters.
7. **A rescued or surrendered population she must look at, name, and interact with as individuals.** Her moral disengagement depends on distance and category; particularity dissolves the category.
8. **Praise framed as choosing her freely, with affection rather than utility.** Counterintuitively destabilizing — she has no template for being valued without being used, and the experience would be unintegrable in real time.
9. **Loss of the Power Cosmic.** Removes the affective flattening; her unmedicated emotional substrate would return in a body that has been chemically and cosmically rewritten beyond recognition. She would be Frankie-at-twenty again, with twenty more years of accumulated unprocessed material, in a body that is not even her impervium-baseline body.
10. **Pregnancy or any forced bodily change she did not author.** Would recapitulate the Horton violation at the somatic register; given that her resolution depended on *re-electing* bodily alteration, an unelected alteration would have no available reframe.

## 5. What Her Collapse Looks Like — The Composite Picture

Drawn together: Frankie does not break loudly. She does not rage, weep, fragment into alters, swing into mania, or turn on her patron. She breaks *quietly*, and in a recognizable sequence — first by working harder, then by speaking in cached phrases, then by leaking affect she cannot name, then by clinging, then by going silent in the middle of a sentence she cannot finish, then by becoming behaviorally absent inside a body that continues to function. The Power Cosmic ensures that her collapse will look, from outside, deceptively undramatic: no obvious physiological signs, no loss of capability, just a progressive emptying of the person who was operating the capability.

The two terminal trajectories are sharp. **Re-capture:** the hollow form is re-authored by the next patron who arrives speaking the right language; she becomes the herald or instrument of someone or something else, perhaps not benign, perhaps catastrophic in its own right. **Hollowing:** no patron arrives in the window, and what remains is a cosmic-class entity executing the script of a self that is no longer present, increasingly uncoupled from any meaning-system, with the moral disengagement she scaffolded as Nova persisting in a form no longer regulated even by devotion.

The single most important entry in this section, for operators: **she will look strongest just before she fails, and she will look almost normal while failing.** Read the cached phrases. Read the over-bright flame. Read the proximity-seeking with the patron. Read the unfinished sentence. By the time conventional indicators of distress would appear in an ordinary person, Frankie will already be at Stage E.

## 6. The Death of 1992, Read As a Failure-Mode Datum

It bears noting that Morg's execution of her in *Silver Surfer* #75 reads, on rewatch, as a failure-mode event the file should not romanticize. She is killed mid-mission, mid-devotion, at the height of her doubling-down curve, by a successor herald — by, in effect, the patron *replacing her with someone more brutal*. She does not get to experience Stage E. The structural collapse is pre-empted by physical death.

This is operationally significant because the canon thereby never tested the personality to destruction. Every failure mode mapped above is *predicted*, not *observed*. The behavioral evidence supporting the prediction is robust — the doubling-down curve, the cached phrases, the categorical brittleness, the bond panic — but the terminal stages are inferential. If she is ever returned to play in a serious extended arc, the file expects the sequence to unfold substantially as described, with the re-capture trajectory marginally more likely than the hollowing trajectory, because the universe she inhabits is densely populated with figures fluent in patron-coded address.

The blunt summary: she was killed before she had to find out what she was without Galactus. That was, in its way, a mercy granted to the character. It was also the loss of the only data point that would have settled the question of whether anything of Frances Raye, the person, survived the resolution she chose at age twenty.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 12: TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT

## Subject: Frances "Frankie" Raye / Nova / Herald-Class

---

## 12.0 Framing Note

Conventional forward assessment presumes a continuous biological subject moving along a developmental arc. With this subject that presumption fails twice. First, she was killed in published canon (decapitation, Morg, *Silver Surfer* #75, 1992) and her trajectory is therefore *interrupted* rather than *concluded*; she exists in a state of latent narrative availability characteristic of Herald-class entities, almost all of whom have at some point returned (Surfer, Firelord, Air-Walker, Terrax, Stardust, Morg himself). Second, even before death, her interior trajectory was being run not by her endocrinology but by the Power Cosmic, which freezes affect in whatever configuration it found at conversion. Forward assessment must therefore work in **two registers**: (a) the trajectory she was on at the moment of death, projected forward as if death had not intervened; (b) the trajectory available to her *if* she is restored, with attention to what restoration mechanism would mean for which version of her returns. These produce different forecasts and different fork points. Both are mapped below.

---

## 12.1 The Trajectory She Was Actually On (1982–1992)

Her ten years of Herald service show a **monotonic, not oscillating, curve**. There is no observable arc of doubt, no inflection toward mercy, no period of questioning followed by re-commitment. The line goes one direction: from a Herald who *accepts* the work (early Nova appearances, *Rom* #65–66, scattered *Silver Surfer* cameos in the Englehart run) to one who *enjoys* the work (mid Starlin run, the Skrull throneworld decision) to one who *evangelizes* the work to the Surfer himself, framing his moral seriousness as a failure of nerve. Projected forward without Morg's intervention, the next inflection was not a crisis of conscience. It was the *consolidation of an ideology* — the construction of an explicit cosmology in which Galactus is not a regrettable necessity but a positive good, and Heralds who serve him with reservations are deficient. She was, at the time of death, in the process of becoming the first Herald to make Galactus's existence *theologically* legible — to herself, then potentially to others.

The probable downstream consequences of this trajectory, had she lived another five to ten publication years:

- **Doctrinal hardening.** A worldview moves from posture to creed by being articulated against opposition. The Surfer was her opposition; further extended encounters would have produced from her something closer to a sermon than a defense. She was likely to become the Herald who spoke, not merely acted.
- **Recruitment posture toward other Heralds.** Morg's recruitment, Stardust's eventual rebellion, the brief Herald-of-the-week period under DeFalco/Marz — in any of these, a living Frankie would have been the senior loyalist in the room, the one explaining to the new arrival how to think about the work. This is consequential: ideologies survive their originators when they are taught.
- **Escalation in target selection.** Her stated criterion for guilt-free worlds (the Skrulls are "monsters") was already a self-serving expansion. The category would have stretched. By the late 1990s a living Nova would plausibly have rationalized worlds chosen for *convenience* (proximity, energy yield) under the same moral cover, the original ethical content draining out of the rationalization while the rationalization remained.
- **A specific collision course with Reed Richards.** Reed enabled her elevation; her trajectory makes him the eventual target of her loyalty-as-grievance. She owes him her cosmic status, and the structure of identification-with-aggressor cases regularly produces a moment in which the survivor turns on the bystander who let it happen. Reed is the only such bystander still alive in her cosmology.
- **No natural off-ramp.** Critically, no internal mechanism existed to slow this curve. Her cognitive style does not ruminate; her defenses do not crack under verbal pressure; her body does not produce the affective signals that would constitute warning. Only an external rupture — power loss, betrayal by Galactus, encounter with Horton's surviving notes — could have bent the line.

Morg's blade therefore did not interrupt a person climbing toward redemption. It interrupted a person climbing toward a more articulate and more dangerous version of what she already was.

---

## 12.2 Resurrection as Fork Point: Who Comes Back Determines Everything

If she returns — and the cosmic-mythos history suggests she eventually will, given the recurrence rate of Herald-class entities — the *mechanism* of return is the single most determinative variable for which Frankie returns. Five plausible mechanisms exist in the established Marvel cosmology, each producing a meaningfully different subject.

**Mechanism A — Galactus restores her directly** (cf. Air-Walker's resurrection patterns; Galactus's known capacity to reconstitute Heralds from residual cosmic signature). The Frankie who returns is the Frankie at the moment of death, unmodified. She wakes mid-ideology, with the additional psychological data point that her patron *wanted her back enough to retrieve her*. This confirms every choice she made. Forecast: the curve resumes from where Morg cut it, accelerated by gratitude. Worst-case outcome on the table.

**Mechanism B — Cosmic entity outside Galactus restores her** (Eternity, the In-Betweener, a resurrection by Adam Warlock during a Soul Gem cycle, etc.). She returns *outside* the bond. This is the only mechanism that even theoretically forces the question her psychology has been organized around avoiding: *who am I when I am not pointed at a target by a larger being?* Forecast bifurcates sharply: either she immediately seeks reattachment to Galactus (high probability, given her structure), or — under sustained interaction with a figure like Warlock who would not let her displace the question — she enters the first genuine developmental crisis of her life. The latter is low-probability but is the single most growth-favorable scenario in the entire dossier.

**Mechanism C — Annihilation-era restoration via residual Power Cosmic** (in the manner of resurrected Heralds in the Abnett/Lanning cosmic period). She returns into a universe at war, with Galactus already in altered states. Forecast: she would seek Galactus, find him changed or absent, and the bond she organized her self around would prove non-restorable in its original form. This is the *catastrophic-growth* fork — growth made possible by enforced separation, but the separation experienced as annihilation of self, with high suicidality-analog risk (Herald-class subjects who lose their patron have historically gone into either rage states (Firelord, post-Galactus) or wandering depressive states (Air-Walker variants)).

**Mechanism D — Restoration as a lesser entity, powers partial or absent.** She returns mortal, or near-mortal. Forecast: this is the only mechanism that returns her to the body that was originally Horton's project — and therefore the only mechanism that re-opens the unprocessed Horton material. Her cosmic exit was the *escape* from that material. Returning her to flesh, particularly to flesh that still bears the impervium substrate, reopens the file. Outcome unpredictable: could collapse her, could finally allow grief, could produce a sustained psychiatric crisis from which she could either build a self or not survive.

**Mechanism E — Restoration as a memory/echo/Power Cosmic residue inhabiting another vessel** (cf. the various Surfer-fragment stories). Not really her. Discarded from this forecast except to note: a fragment-Frankie loose in the cosmos, carrying the ideology without the biography, is its own threat vector.

The dossier's central forward-assessment finding is this: **whether she grows or worsens depends almost entirely on whether her return reattaches her to Galactus or separates her from him.** Reattached, she is the trajectory of §12.1 resumed. Separated, she is forced into the only developmental work she has never done.

---

## 12.3 The Open Questions

These are the unsettled items in the file — points where the evidence does not yet permit a confident reading and where any future appearance would be diagnostically rich.

1. **Did she ever, even once, doubt?** The published record shows no such moment. But the published record is sparse for long stretches of her Herald years; the file cannot rule out a private moment that was never depicted. Any future flashback writer who places a single scene of doubt in her past changes the diagnosis materially — from monotonic ideologue to a person who suppressed doubts, which is a more workable starting position for growth.
2. **What did she know about Galactus's previous Heralds when she volunteered?** If she knew the Surfer's biography in detail — exile, regret, eventual rebellion — and volunteered anyway, the volunteering reads as informed self-selection into a known role. If she knew only that the role existed, it reads as something closer to flight without map. Her later contempt for the Surfer suggests the former; she had to have been told, and disagreed with his choices in advance.
3. **What, exactly, is the residual Horton material doing inside the Power Cosmic substrate?** The Power Cosmic does not erase prior memory; it recolors affect. The Horton file is still in there, walled off but present. Under what stimulus does the wall fail? This is the unknown most relevant to any future writer engaging her seriously.
4. **Is the contempt for the Surfer also envy?** The dossier (§5) reads it primarily as defensive — his hesitation questions her resolution. But envy is also possible: he retains the moral interiority she traded away. If envy is in the mixture, it constitutes a tiny leak in the structure that could, under pressure, widen.
5. **What is her relationship to the name "Frances"?** She is "Frankie" in the human period; she is "Nova" in the cosmic period. The full given name appears almost nowhere. A subject who has shed her own first name twice may be more recoverable through it than through either of her adopted ones — naming work is one of the few interventions available in a case this structurally compromised.
6. **Would Johnny Storm's voice still reach her?** Almost certainly not through a Galactus-restored Frankie. Possibly through a mortal-restored Frankie (§12.2 Mechanism D), and Johnny is one of perhaps three people in the universe whose presence she could not write off as moral weakness, because his presence indexes her one period of relative ordinary happiness. This is a fork point with a name attached.

---

## 12.4 The Fork Points (Decisional Topology)

Mapping the next decade of any restored Frankie's life as a branching tree:

**Fork 1 — Reattachment or not.** Resolved by mechanism of return (§12.2). All downstream forks depend on this. Reattached: skip to §12.1's resumed trajectory. Not reattached: continue.

**Fork 2 — Solitude tolerance.** A non-reattached Frankie must spend some interval alone with herself, possibly the first such interval of her life. She either (a) finds the solitude unbearable and immediately seeks a substitute patron (likely candidates: any cosmic-scale entity that will have her — the In-Betweener, a restored Tyrant, even an Annihilus-class warlord — the *content* of the patron matters less than the structure), or (b) tolerates the solitude, badly. (a) is high-probability and produces a Frankie effectively identical to the Nova of §12.1 wearing a new uniform. (b) is the low-probability door to growth.

**Fork 3 — The Horton confrontation.** If (b) at Fork 2, the unprocessed material surfaces. She either (a) re-walls it (returning her to Fork 2a), or (b) sits with it. (b) requires either a therapeutic relationship (no plausible candidate in her cosmology — the closest is the Surfer, whom she has poisoned against herself) or a forced confinement (cosmic prison, depowering, the kind of imposed stillness she has spent her entire post-revelation life avoiding).

**Fork 4 — Atonement vs. integration.** If she ever does confront her Nova-era actions, she faces the standard survivor-perpetrator's fork: atone (which can become its own self-annihilating performance, structurally identical to her devotion to Galactus, with the polarity reversed), or integrate (acknowledge without performance, hold both the courage and the cruelty as her own, find proportionate amends). She is at high risk for the atonement pattern — it would feel familiar, it would supply a role, it would give her a larger figure (the wronged) to orient toward. Integration is the harder and more genuine path, and her cognitive style (low introspection, action-orientation) actively works against it.

**Fork 5 — Recurrence.** Even if she grows, she remains vulnerable to re-recruitment by any sufficiently large patron. The template laid down by Horton does not erase; it can only be *complicated* by competing experiences. A grown Frankie is a Frankie who has built additional structures alongside the original template, not one who has demolished it. Lifelong vigilance for re-recruitment scenarios would be indicated.

---

## 12.5 What Would Push Her Toward Growth

Specific, granular, in descending order of plausibility and ascending order of efficacy:

- **Forced power loss.** Nothing else removes the affect-suppression of the Power Cosmic. Until she feels human endocrinology again, the grief that should have followed the Horton revelation cannot run. Power loss is the precondition.
- **A confinement environment with no role to perform.** She has never been observed simply existing without an assignment. A period of enforced stillness — cosmic prison, exile to a single small world, depowered convalescence — would force the encounter she has spent her life avoiding.
- **Access to Horton's actual notes.** Reading, in his own hand, the specifications of what he did to her — including the procedural details her hypnotic blocks never let her witness — would make the abstraction concrete. Concrete content is what her defenses cannot easily recategorize.
- **A reunion with Johnny that is not a confrontation.** Not an argument about her choices — she would win that argument with herself in advance. A reunion in which Johnny simply treats her as Frankie, uses her actual name, references shared small moments from the FF#164–#244 period (the diner they went to, the way she would not let him cook, the night she finally let him hold her without flinching), would do more than any moral challenge. The pre-Nova self has to be *re-evidenced* to her before she can mourn what was done to it.
- **Sustained contact with the Surfer in a context where she cannot leave.** Long-arc work, not a single scene. The Surfer's moral seriousness is the only mirror she has reliably found uncomfortable. Discomfort, sustained, is a developmental nutrient.
- **A child.** Speculative and contingent on Mechanism D restoration, but: a person whose pathology is rooted in caregiver-as-experimenter would be powerfully reorganized by the experience of being trusted by something small that did not deserve to be experimented on. The risk of repetition is also present; this is a high-variance intervention.
- **Encounter with a Skrull survivor of the world she helped destroy** — by name, by biography, with a face. The Skrull genocide is the keystone of her moral disengagement; particularizing one of the dead would attack the keystone directly.

---

## 12.6 What Would Push Her Toward Catastrophe

- **Galactus's restoration of her, full-powered, with expressed gratitude.** As above: confirms the structure, accelerates the curve.
- **A new patron of comparable or greater scale.** Tyrant, a restored Maelstrom, an ascended Annihilus, the Beyonders, even the right cosmic-tier Asgardian — any of these, if they offered her the Galactus-position, would receive her. The fact that her devotion is structural rather than person-specific is itself the danger.
- **A successful sermon.** If she ever recruits another Herald to her *ideology* (as opposed to her side in a fight), the ideology becomes self-reinforcing through teaching. Articulation hardens it further; she becomes unreachable.
- **Death of the Surfer.** He is the only Herald-peer whose existence pressures her. Without him, the field of equals in which she might be questioned empties.
- **Validation by a moral authority.** Counterintuitive but real: if any figure she could not dismiss as weak (a cosmic-tier Captain Universe, a Living Tribunal aspect, a restored Watcher in advisory mode) ever expressed even partial sympathy with the necessity of Galactus, she would receive it as absolution and the structure would calcify permanently.
- **Encounter with a deeply broken version of Johnny.** If Johnny were diminished — bereaved, broken, lesser than she remembers — her contempt for human weakness would consume the one bond capable of reaching her.
- **Re-encounter with Horton's living legacy (a successor experimenter, an inheritor of his work).** She would either annihilate the inheritor (re-enacting the rage she never directed at Horton himself, briefly cathartic but structurally inert) or, more dangerously, *recruit* the inheritor — make them her Reed Richards, the technician who serves her now as Reed served her once.

---

## 12.7 The Single Most Probable Forward Path

Weighting all factors — the high return rate of Herald-class entities, Galactus's documented preference for restoring useful instruments, the trajectory she was on at death, the absence of any internal growth mechanism — the single most probable forward path for this subject is:

> Restoration by Galactus or a Galactus-proxy. Reattachment within minutes of return. Resumption of the §12.1 curve, now with the additional data point that she has survived death in service. Hardening into the *theological* phase: she becomes the Herald who explains. Probable confrontation with a returned Surfer in which she is not persuaded. Probable role in a future cosmic-scale conflict on Galactus's side. Probable second death, possibly definitive, possibly in a moment that finally — in the last seconds — lets the wall fall.

This forecast is grim and is offered without satisfaction. It reflects the structure as it stands, not as the dossier's author wishes it stood.

---

## 12.8 The Growth Path That Would Surprise Everyone

Held open for completeness, because forecasts of human (and post-human) systems should never close the door on the low-probability good outcome.

A Frankie restored outside the bond, depowered, named *Frances* by someone who knew her before, given time without a mission and a single concrete piece of evidence of what was done to her in childhood — would have, perhaps, a year of unbearable months. At the end of that year there is a non-zero probability of the first genuinely authored self she has ever possessed. It would not look like the Nova who blazed through the Skrull throneworld; it would not look like the cheerful Torch-girlfriend; it would not look like the recoiling child Horton built. It would look like a woman in early middle age, quiet, slow to speak, capable of grief, no longer in service to anyone, and — for the first time in her life — capable of choosing what fire to walk into.

The probability is low. The value of the outcome is high. The dossier registers it as the one thing worth working toward, should any agency capable of working toward it ever take an interest in this file.

---

*End Section 12. See §13 (Counterintelligence: Manipulation Vulnerabilities & Recruitment Vectors) for adversary-side mirror of this assessment.*
